والظُّلُ الذي في هذا الوقت هو في الزَّوال ، فإذا زالَ الظَّلُ من هذا الخطّ إذن ينبغي أن تراعى عدة أمور ليقرب العمل من التحقيق، كأن يكون الشمس في الانقلاب الصيفي أو قريباً منه لبطء حركة الميل المخل بالموازاة هناك، وكون الظل أبينُ في الصيف لصفاء الهواء وشدة الشعاعِ وقلّة عوارض الجو المانعة من أخذ الظل. وأن لا تكون قريبة من الأفق ؛ إذ لا يتحقق أطرافُ الظل عند ذلك لتشتتها، ولا من نصف النهار ؛ لبطوء تقلّص الظلّ هناك وانبساطه ، فلا يتعين وقت الدخولُ والخروج. فإذا روعي هذه الشرائط تحفظ الموازاة بقدر الإمكان، ويتبين الظل، ويسلم عن تشتت طرفه وبطوء حركته». انتهى. وذكر شراح تشريح الأفلاك وغيرهم أنّ من مسالك استخراج الخطين المذكورين أن ي ن يخرج من قاعدة المقياس خط مستقيم على استقامة الظل قبل نصف النهار، ويؤخذ الارتفاع في تلك الحالة، ثم ينظر بعد نصف النهار فإذا صار الارتفاعُ مثل الارتفاع الأوّل يخرجُ من القاعدة خط آخر على استقامة الظل، فيحصل في الأغلب زاوية، وتنصف تلك الزاوية، فالخط المنصف . هو خط نصف النهار. ومنها : أن يرصد الظل للمقياس قبل نصف النهار، ويُعَلِّمُ على رأسه علامة، ثمّ يرصد الظل بعد نصف النهار إلى أن صار مثل الظلّ الأوّل، ويُعَلِّمُ على رأسه علامة، ويوصل بين العلامتين بخط مستقيم، ويقام على ذلك الخط عمود، فهو خط نصف النهار. ومنها : أن يستخرج خطّ على امتدادِ ظلّ المقياس عند طلوع الشمس وغروبها في يوم واحد بخطين، وتنصفُ الزاوية الواقعة بينهما فهو خط نصف النهار. [1] قوله : هو فيء الزوال ؛ الفيء في اللغة بمعنى الرجوع، وهو من أسماء الظل مطلقاً، سمي به لرجوعِهِ من جانب إلى جانب، ومنهم من يخصه بما بعد الزوال، وما قبل الزوال يخص باسم الظلّ، وهذا الظلّ الذي هو عند استواء الشمس على نصف النهار، واستواء ظل المقياس على خط نصف النهار إنما سمي بفيء الزوال ؛ لأنّ الزوال متّصل به ، فإضافة الفيء إلى الزوال لأدنى ملابسته.  فهو وقت الزوال [١] عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية فإنَّ المراد بفيء الزوال ظلّ الأشياء عندما تكون الشمس على نصف النهار، وزوال الشمس من نصف النهار إلى جانب الغرب يكون بعده بلا واسطة، كذا ذكره البرجندي في حواشي شرح ملخص الجغميني». وهذا يرشدك إلى أنّ الزوالَ عندهم عبارة عن ميلان الشمس من وسط السماء إلى جانب المغرب، وأما قيامه على دائرة نصف النهار في وسط السماء، فيقال له : الاستواء، وهذا هو المناسب بالنسبة إلى المعنى اللغوي، وهو المستعمل غالباً في الإطلاقات الشرعية. وقد يطلق الزوال على نفس الاستواء أيضاً كما ذكره جمع من محشي الشرح المذكور، وعليه فإضافة الفيء إلى الزوالِ مستقيمة بلا تكلّف، وبهذا اندفع التعارض بين قول بعض الفقهاء أنّ أوّل وقت الظهر هو أوّل الزوال، وبين قول بعض آخرين : إن وقته بعد الزوال ولو بدقيقة، وذلك لأنَّ المراد بالزوالِ في قول الأولين هو المعنى الأول، وفي قول الآخرين هو المعنى الثاني. ويمكن أن يراد بالزوال في قول الآخرين أيضاً هو المعنى الأول، ويقصد به الزوال النفس الأمري، بناءً على ما قال محمود بن إلياس الرومي في «شرح مختصر الوقاية»: «فإذا زالت الشمس على منتهى الارتفاع أخذ الظلّ في الزيادة، فمن حيث صارت الزيادة مدركة بالحس دخل أوّل وقت الظهر، ويعلم قطعاً أن الزوال في علم الله وقع قبله، لكن التكاليف لا ترتبط إلا بما تدخل تحت الحس). [١] قوله : فهو وقت الزوال ؛ هذا إذا كان قدر من الظل باقياً عند الاستواء، كما في أكثر البلاد الشمالية التي لا تَصِلُ الشمس فيها على سمتِ الرأس، بل تكون جنوبية حين وصولها على دائرة نصف النهار. وأما البلاد التي تصل الشمس فيها على سمتِ الرأس في السنة مرة أو مرتين فالزوالُ يعرف بزيادة الظلّ على فيء الزوال في غير ذينك اليومين، وفي ذينك اليومين
The shadow at this time is at the time of decline, so when the shadow has moved from this line, several things should be observed to bring the action close to accuracy: such as the sun being at the summer solstice or near it because of the slowness of the motion of inclination that disturbs parallelism there, and the shadow being clearer in summer due to clear air and intense rays and the few atmospheric obstructions preventing taking the shadow. And that it should not be close to the horizon, because the ends of the shadow are not realized then due to their dispersion, nor close to noon, because of the slowness of the contraction and expansion of the shadow there, so the time of entry and exit is not determined. When these conditions are observed, parallelism is preserved as much as possible, the shadow becomes clear, and it is safe from dispersion of its end and slowness of its motion. End. The commentators of Tashrih al-Aflak and others mentioned that among the methods of extracting the two mentioned lines is that a straight line is drawn from the base of the gnomon along the direction of the shadow before noon, and the altitude is taken at that state, then after noon it is observed; when the altitude becomes like the first altitude, another line is drawn from the base along the direction of the shadow, thus an angle is usually obtained, and that angle is bisected; the bisecting line is the meridian line. Also: the shadow of the gnomon is observed before noon, and a mark is made on its head, then the shadow is observed after noon until it becomes like the first shadow, and a mark is made on its head, and a straight line is drawn between the two marks, and a perpendicular is erected on that line; that is the meridian line. Also: a line is drawn along the extension of the shadow of the gnomon at sunrise and sunset on one day with two lines, and the angle between them is bisected; that is the meridian line. [1] His saying: it is the shadow of decline; al-fay' linguistically means return, and it is a name for shadow absolutely, named for its return from side to side. Some restrict it to after decline, and what is before decline is called shadow specifically. This shadow which is at the time of the sun's alignment with the meridian and the alignment of the gnomon's shadow on the meridian line is only called the shadow of decline because decline is connected to it, so adding 'shadow' to 'decline' is due to the least relation. [PAGE_010] So it is the time of decline. 'Umdat al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya. Indeed, what is meant by the shadow of decline is the shadow of objects when the sun is at the meridian, and the sun's decline from the meridian to the west occurs immediately after, as mentioned by al-Birjandi in his glosses on Sharh Talkhis al-Jighmini. This guides you that decline according to them is an expression for the sun's inclination from the middle of the sky to the west, whereas its standing on the meridian circle in the middle of the sky is called alignment. This is appropriate with respect to the linguistic meaning, and it is commonly used in Shariah usages. Sometimes decline is also applied to alignment itself, as mentioned by a group of glossators on the aforementioned commentary. Accordingly, adding 'shadow' to 'decline' is straightforward without difficulty. This resolves the apparent contradiction between some jurists saying that the beginning of zuhr time is the beginning of decline, and others saying that its time is after decline even by a minute. This is because what is meant by decline in the statement of the first group is the first meaning, and in the statement of the others is the second meaning. It is also possible that decline in the statement of the others refers to the first meaning, intending the actual decline, based on what Mahmud ibn Ilyas al-Rumi said in 'Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya': 'When the sun has declined at the peak of altitude, the shadow begins to increase. From the point where the increase is perceptible, the beginning of zuhr time enters, and it is known with certainty that the decline happened before that in the knowledge of God, but obligations are only connected to what falls under sensation.' [1] His saying: so it is the time of decline; this is if some shadow remains at alignment, as in most northern countries where the sun never reaches the zenith, but is south when it reaches the meridian circle. As for countries where the sun reaches the zenith once or twice a year, decline is known by the increase of shadow beyond the shadow of decline on days other than those two, and on those two days
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling from a Hanafi commentary on Sharh al-Wiqaya. It addresses the determination of the start time of Zuhr prayer by defining the technical term 'فيء الزوال' (fay' al-zawal) and explaining the astronomical methods for determining the meridian line and the onset of decline. The author discusses the linguistic and technical meanings of 'ظل' (shadow) and 'زوال' (decline), noting that 'فيء' originally means 'return' and can refer to any shadow, but some restrict it to the shadow after noon. The key ruling is that Zuhr time begins when the sun has actually declined from its zenith, but since this decline is imperceptible to the unaided senses, the beginning of Zuhr is known by the increase of the shadow after its shortest length. This resolves the apparent disagreement among Hanafi jurists: some say Zuhr begins at the first moment of decline, others say after a minute. This is reconciled by noting that the first group refers to the actual decline in divine knowledge, while the second refers to the perceptible onset. The passage emphasizes that Shariah obligations are contingent on sensory perception. The commentary further clarifies that in most northern regions, some shadow always remains at noon, so decline is recognized by the increase of shadow. In equatorial regions where the sun reaches the zenith, the ruling is nuanced: on the days of zenith, the shadow increases from nothing, so the same principle applies.

Key Terms
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawal): The shadow of an object when the sun is at the meridian, i.e., at its zenith. It is called 'shadow of decline' because decline immediately follows.
زوال (zawal): The sun's decline from the meridian towards the west. Sometimes also used synonymously with alignment (i.e., the moment just before decline).
خط نصف النهار (khatt nisf al-nahar): The meridian line, a north-south line that indicates when the sun is at its highest point. Used to determine noon and the shadow of decline.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the time for Zuhr prayer begin?
A) Exactly when the sun passes the meridian (actual decline).
B) When the shadow starts to increase after its shortest length (perceptible decline).
C) When the sun is at the zenith.
D) When the shadow of an object is exactly the same as its height.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines the start of Zuhr prayer by the perceptible increase of shadow after its shortest length, not the imperceptible moment of decline.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
10 min
Definition of Zawal and the Beginning of Zuhr Time
Clarifying the meaning of zawal and its relation to Zuhr time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of zawal, explain the apparent contradiction about Zuhr start time, and identify the primary evidences from Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
Zawal is the sun's decline from the zenith; Zuhr begins at the first perceptible increase of shadow.

Prayer times are tied to the movement of the sun. Knowing exactly when Zuhr begins requires precision. Hanafi scholars clarified that 'zawal' — the decline of the sun from its highest point — is the trigger. But you may find conflicting statements: some say Zuhr starts at zawal, others after zawal. This lesson resolves that confusion and grounds the ruling in foundational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish zawal from istiwa'
Identify that 'zawal' technically refers to the sun's decline from the meridian, while 'istiwa'' is the moment at the zenith. The passage notes that some scholars loosely use 'zawal' for the zenith, causing confusion.
2
Resolve the apparent contradiction
Two groups of jurists: one says Zuhr starts at 'first zawal', another says 'after zawal'. By clarifying the two meanings of 'zawal', the contradiction disappears. The first group means the decline, the second group means the zenith.
Alternatively, the second group refers to the actual divine moment, but legal obligation is based on sensory perception.
3
Apply the sensory principle
The passage emphasizes that legal obligations (taklif) are linked to what is perceptible by the senses. Thus, the first time of Zuhr is when the shadow begins to increase — the first sign of decline.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle: ahkam are based on the apparent, not the hidden.
4
Review the proofs
Two main evidences: Quran 17:78 ('duluk al-shams' interpreted as zawal by Ibn 'Umar) and the hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet in prayer, where he prayed Zuhr when the sun declined (malat).
These are the primary dalil for the ruling.

فهو وقت الزوال
[1]
عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية
فإنَّ المراد بفيء الزوال ظلّ الأشياء عندما تكون الشمس على نصف النهار، وزوال الشمس من نصف النهار إلى جانب الغرب يكون بعده بلا واسطة، كذا ذكره البرجندي في حواشي شرح ملخص الجغميني».
وهذا يرشدك إلى أنّ الزوالَ عندهم عبارة عن ميلان الشمس من وسط السماء إلى جانب المغرب، وأما قيامه على دائرة نصف النهار في وسط السماء، فيقال له : الاستواء، وهذا هو المناسب بالنسبة إلى المعنى اللغوي، وهو المستعمل غالباً في الإطلاقات الشرعية.
وقد يطلق الزوال على نفس الاستواء أيضاً كما ذكره جمع من محشي الشرح المذكور، وعليه فإضافة الفيء إلى الزوالِ مستقيمة بلا تكلّف، وبهذا اندفع التعارض بين قول بعض الفقهاء أنّ أوّل وقت الظهر هو أوّل الزوال، وبين قول بعض آخرين : إن وقته بعد الزوال ولو بدقيقة، وذلك لأنَّ المراد بالزوالِ في قول الأولين هو المعنى الأول، وفي قول الآخرين هو المعنى الثاني.
ويمكن أن يراد بالزوال في قول الآخرين أيضاً هو المعنى الأول، ويقصد به الزوال النفس الأمري، بناءً على ما قال محمود بن إلياس الرومي في «شرح مختصر الوقاية»: «فإذا زالت الشمس على منتهى الارتفاع أخذ الظلّ في الزيادة، فمن حيث صارت الزيادة مدركة بالحس دخل أوّل وقت الظهر، ويعلم قطعاً أن الزوال في علم الله وقع قبله، لكن التكاليف لا ترتبط إلا بما تدخل تحت الحس).
[1] قوله : فهو وقت الزوال ؛ هذا إذا كان قدر من الظل باقياً عند الاستواء، كما في أكثر البلاد الشمالية التي لا تَصِلُ الشمس فيها على سمتِ الرأس، بل تكون جنوبية حين وصولها على دائرة نصف النهار.
وأما البلاد التي تصل الشمس فيها على سمتِ الرأس في السنة مرة أو مرتين فالزوالُ يعرف بزيادة الظلّ على فيء الزوال في غير ذينك اليومين، وفي ذينك اليومين
(۱) في «شرح النقاية»(ص٣٤): ووقع في قلبه. (۲) انتهى من شرح النقاية» لإلياس زاده (ص٣٤).

فذلك أول وقت الظهر

۱۱
اللذين تصل الشمس فيها على سمتِ الرأس لا يكون للمقياس ظلّ عند الاستواء ، فيعرف الزوال بحدوثه بعد فنائه.
١ ] قوله فذلك أوّل وقت الظهر ؛ أي وقت الزوال هو ابتداء وقت الظهر، وما في «ملخص الخغميني»: «إذا انتهى الظلّ الثاني ؛ أي الظلّ المستوي نهايته عند غاية ارتفاع الشمس، فهو أول الظهر». انتهى.
فهو سهو ظاهر ؛ لأنَّ أوّل وقت الظهر ليس وقت الاستواء، بل بعيده اتفاقاً إلا أن يقال : هو مبني على أنّ أوّل الشيء خارج عن الشيء، وأما ما قال شارحه قاضي زاده: «إنّ أوّل وقته بعد الزوال بالاتفاق». انتهى. فإنّ حمل الزوال في كلامه على الاستواء كما ذكرنا سابقاً فهو صحيح، وإلا ففساده ظاهر، والأولى أن يقول: بعيد الاستواء.

وغيره.
ألفاظه : عن جابر بن عبد الله له ، قال : جاء جبريل إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حين مالت الشمس، فقال : قم يا محمد فصل، فصلى الظهر حين مالت الشمس ، ثم مكث حتى إذا كان فيء الرجل مثله ، جاءه للعصر فقال : قم يا محمد فصل العصر ، ثم مكث حتى إذا غابت الشمس جاءه ، فقال : قم فصل المغرب، فقام فصلاها، ثم مكث حتى إذا غاب الشفق جاءه
So it is the time of zawal. [1] 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. The intended meaning of the 'shadow of zawal' is the shadow of objects when the sun is at the meridian, and the declination of the sun from the meridian to the west occurs immediately after it. This is how al-Birjandi mentioned it in his gloss on Sharh Talkhis al-Jighmini. This guides you to the fact that 'zawal' according to them is an expression for the sun's inclination from the middle of the sky towards the west. As for its standing on the meridian circle in the middle of the sky, it is called 'istiwa'' (the sun at zenith). This is appropriate in relation to the linguistic meaning, and it is commonly used in Islamic legal terminology. Sometimes 'zawal' is also applied to the very same 'istiwa'' as mentioned by a group of glossators on the aforementioned commentary. Accordingly, the addition of 'shadow' to 'zawal' is straightforward without any strain. By this, the apparent contradiction between the statement of some jurists that 'the first time of Zhuhr is the first moment of zawal' and the statement of others that 'its time is after zawal, even by a minute' is resolved. This is because (the term) 'zawal' in the first group's statement refers to the first meaning, and in the other group's statement it refers to the second meaning. It is also possible that 'zawal' in the statement of the others refers to the first meaning, but intended is the essential 'zawal' (in God's knowledge). Based on what Mahmud ibn Ilyas al-Rumi said in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah: 'When the sun inclines at its maximum height, the shadow begins to increase. From the point where the increase becomes perceptible by the senses, the first time of Zhuhr enters. It is known with certainty that the actual zawal in God's knowledge occurred before that, but legal obligations are only linked to what falls under sensory perception.' [1] His statement: 'So it is the time of zawal' – this applies when some shadow remains at the time of istiwa', as is the case in most northern regions where the sun does not reach the zenith, but rather is to the south when it reaches the meridian circle. As for regions where the sun reaches the zenith once or twice a year, zawal is known by the increase of the shadow beyond the shadow of zawal on days other than those two. On those two days when the sun reaches the zenith, there is no shadow for the gnomon at istiwa', so zawal is known by its occurrence after its disappearance. [1] His statement: 'That is the first time of Zhuhr' – meaning the time of zawal is the beginning of the time of Zhuhr. What is in Talkhis al-Jighmini: 'When the second shadow – i.e., the shadow that is level, its end at the sun's maximum height – ends, that is the first time of Zhuhr.' End quote. This is an apparent oversight, because the first time of Zhuhr is not the time of istiwa' but rather after it by agreement. Unless one says: It is based on the principle that the beginning of a thing is outside the thing. As for what its commentator Qadi Zadah said: 'Its first time is after zawal by consensus' – end quote. If he intended 'zawal' in his statement to mean 'istiwa'' as we mentioned previously, then it is correct; otherwise, its incorrectness is apparent. It is better to say: 'after istiwa'. The evidence that the first time of Zhuhr is zawal is His statement, exalted is He: 'Establish prayer at the decline of the sun' (17:78). Ibn 'Umar interpreted it as zawal (declination). This is narrated from him by Malik in al-Muwatta', 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba, Ibn Jarir, Ibn al-Mundhir and others, as we have elaborated with mention of the differing narrations in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' Muhammad. And the hadith of Jibril's leadership on the morning of the night of Mi'raj, as narrated by al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, Ishaq, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Khuzayma, al-Hakim, al-Daraqutni, al-Nasa'i, Abu Dawud, and Ibn Hibban and others. Among its wordings: from Jabir ibn 'Abd Allah, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: Jibril came to the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) when the sun had declined (malat), and said: 'Stand, O Muhammad, and pray.' So he prayed Zhuhr when the sun had declined. Then he waited until the shadow of a man was like his height, and came for 'Asr and said: 'Stand, O Muhammad, and pray.' So he prayed 'Asr. Then he waited until the sun set, and came and said: 'Stand and pray Maghrib.' So he stood and prayed it. Then he waited until the twilight disappeared, and came...
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of 'zawal' (the sun's decline) and its relation to the beginning of the time for Zuhr prayer. The author first clarifies that 'zawal' in the context of prayer times refers to the moment when the sun begins to incline from its zenith (istiwa) towards the west. This is distinguished from the zenith itself, which is called 'istiwa'. The commentator notes that some scholars use 'zawal' loosely to mean the zenith, which caused an apparent conflict: some say Zuhr starts at zawal, others say after zawal. The resolution is that the first group means the decline, while the second group uses 'zawal' to mean the zenith, so Zuhr actually starts after that moment. Alternatively, the second group might refer to the actual divine moment of decline, but legal obligations are based on sensory perception (i.e., when the shadow begins to increase). The passage then addresses the anomaly of regions near the equator where the sun is directly overhead, and how zawal is determined there. Finally, it provides the primary textual evidence: the Quranic verse 'Aqim al-salah li-duluk al-shams' interpreted by Ibn 'Umar as the sun's decline, and the hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet in prayer at the five times, starting Zuhr when the sun declined. Thus, the Hanafi position is firmly established: the first time of Zuhr is at the beginning of the sun's decline from its meridian.

Key Terms
الزوال (al-zawal): The sun's inclination from the meridian (zenith) towards the west; the first moment of its decline.
الاستواء (al-istiwa'): The sun being at the meridian, i.e., at its highest point in the sky at midday.
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawal): The shadow that objects cast when the sun is at the zenith (meridian); also called 'the shadow of zawal'.
دلوك الشمس (duluk al-shams): The sun's decline from the meridian; interpreted by Ibn 'Umar as zawal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the time for Zuhr prayer begin?
A) When the sun is at its zenith (istiwa').
B) When the sun begins to decline (zawal), at the first perceptible increase of shadow.
C) When the shadow of an object becomes equal to its height.
D) When the sun has completely set.

Key Takeaway
Zuhr time begins at the first perceptible increase of shadow after the sun declines from its zenith — this is the Hanafi definition of zawal.

The Beginning of Zuhr: Zawal as the Start Time
Ruling on start of Zuhr with Quran and Hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the beginning of Zuhr time according to the Hanafi school and cite the Quranic evidence (Isra 78 interpreted by Ibn Umar) and the hadith of Jibril that support this, while explaining why the time is after zawal, not at solar noon.

Core Idea
Zuhr begins when the sun declines from its zenith (zawal), not at the moment of highest sun.

Knowing the precise start of Zuhr prayer is essential for correct worship. The Hanafi school, based on clear Quranic and sunna evidence, holds that Zuhr begins when the sun has passed its zenith and begins to decline—a moment known as zawal. In this lesson, we examine the authoritative ruling, the evidence, and a common misconception that places the start at solar noon.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The author explicitly says: 'So that is the beginning of Zuhr time' referring to zawal. Understand that the beginning of Zuhr is the moment of zawal, i.e., the sun's decline after reaching its zenith.
This is the established Hanafi position.
2
Identify the precise moment
Zawal is known by the shadow's behavior: at noon the shadow is at its shortest (or absent), and zawal is when a shadow begins to appear on the opposite side. The author refutes the idea that Zuhr starts at the end of the 'second shadow' (a misinterpretation).
The critique of Mukhtasar al-Khaghimini highlights this mistake.
3
Recognize the critique of an erroneous view
The author points out that a statement from Mukhtasar al-Khaghimini (suggesting Zuhr begins when the straight shadow ends) is an oversight. He clarifies that the beginning is not at the moment of equinox (istawa) but after it, by consensus.
Also addresses Qadi Zadah's comment, clarifying that if 'zawal' is misread as equinox, it is wrong.
4
Cite the primary Quranic evidence
Allah says: 'Establish prayer at the decline of the sun' (Isra 78). The companion Ibn Umar interpreted 'duluk' as 'zawal', as recorded in Malik's Muwatta and other collections. This interpretation is accepted by the Hanafi school.
The word 'duluk' is the key linguistic evidence.
5
Support with the hadith of Jibril
The famous hadith relates that Jibril came to the Prophet when 'the sun had tilted' (i.e., after zawal) and led him in Zuhr. This confirms the start time is after the sun's zenith.
The hadith is narrated by many scholars including al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and al-Tirmidhi.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the beginning of Zuhr time with its proof. The author starts by stating that the beginning of Zuhr is at zawal (the sun's decline from the zenith). He then critiques a statement from 'Mukhtasar al-Khaghimini' that suggests the beginning is at the moment the second shadow ends (a concept related to the noon shadow). He clarifies that this is mistaken because Zuhr begins after noon, not at it. He also addresses Qadi Zadah's comment, pointing out that if by 'zawal' Qadi Zadah meant the equinox (exact noon), then it's wrong; if he meant the decline after noon, it's correct. The author then provides evidence from the Quran (Surah al-Isra, verse 78: 'Establish prayer at the decline of the sun'), which Ibn Umar interpreted as zawal. This is supported by the famous hadith of Jibril, where Jibril led the Prophet in prayer at the beginning of each time; for Zuhr, he came when the sun had tilted (i.e., after zawal). This establishes that the beginning of Zuhr is after the sun's zenith.

Key Terms
زوال (zawal): The sun's declination from the zenith; the moment when the shadow begins to appear after being absent at noon.
دلوك الشمس (duluk al-shams): The decline of the sun; interpreted as zawal by Ibn Umar and the Hanafi school.

Zuhr time begins immediately after the sun's zenith, known as zawal, as established by Quran, hadith, and consensus.

End of Zuhr Time and Method of Determining Zawal
Ruling on end of Zuhr and zawal method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the end of Zuhr time, including the role of the zawal shadow, and explain the practical method for determining the moment of zawal using a measuring stick.

Core Idea
Zuhr ends when the shadow of a stick reaches twice its length, accounting for the residual shadow at midday.

Prayer times are defined by precise environmental markers. This lesson presents the Hanafi school's definition of the end of Zuhr time, which involves measuring the shadow of a stick. It also provides a simple experimental method to determine the moment of zawal—when the sun passes its zenith—using the same stick. Understanding these rules ensures that Zuhr is performed within its valid period, as performing it after this boundary would require making it up later.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time condition
The passage concerns the end of Zuhr prayer time. This is a temporal condition (shart) for the validity of Zuhr.
2
Understand the measurement formula
The end is when the shadow of a vertical stick (mizwad) equals twice the stick's length, but you must add the shadow that was present at zawal (the moment of midday).
This addition is unique to the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the example
If the shadow at zawal is a quarter of the stick, then the end of Zuhr is when the total shadow reaches two and a quarter stick lengths.
The formula: end = 2 × stick + zawal shadow.
4
Consider the exception
If there is no shadow at noon (e.g., at the equator when the sun is directly overhead), then the end is simply twice the stick alone.
This case is rare but shows the principle's flexibility.
5
Learn the experimental method for zawal
To determine zawal, erect a straight stick on level ground. As long as the shadow shortens, the sun is rising. When the shadow stops shortening and becomes steady (the shortest point), that is the moment of zawal.
After zawal, the shadow begins to lengthen again.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the end of Zuhr time and a practical method for determining zawal. The author states that the end of Zuhr is when the shadow of a measuring stick (mizwad) becomes equal to twice the length of the stick, after subtracting the shadow that existed at zawal. For example, if the shadow at zawal ('fay' al-zawal') is a quarter of the stick, then the end of Zuhr is when the shadow reaches two and a quarter times the stick. The commentary explains that this is based on the condition that a shadow exists at noon; if there is no shadow at noon (e.g., at the equator when the sun is directly overhead), then the end is simply when the shadow is twice the stick. There is a subtle discussion about whether the 'end' of a time includes the boundary moment or not, and the commentator resolves that it refers to the moment when the next time begins. Finally, a method for identifying zawal is given from 'al-Kifayah': erect a straight stick on level ground; as long as the shadow is shortening, the sun is rising; when the shadow becomes steady (starts to lengthen after the shortest point), that is zawal.

Key Terms
مقياس (midyas): A straight stick erected to measure shadows and determine the sun's position.
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawal): The shadow length at the moment of zawal (sun's declination). This is subtracted from the total when computing the end of Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines the end of Zuhr by adding the shadow at zawal to twice the stick's length, a precision necessary for accurate prayer times.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the End Time of Zuhr Prayer
Defines end of Zuhr time and presents two narrations from Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two narrations from Abu Hanifa on the end time of Zuhr and explain why the majority of Hanafi scholars prefer the first narration.

Core Idea
Two narrations from Abu Hanifa on Zuhr's end; the preferred one is when shadow doubles, not equals.

The end time of Zuhr prayer is a matter of scholarly detail within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Hanifa himself transmitted two different opinions on when Zuhr ends. This lesson examines those two views, the evidence cited for each, and which position became the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling. Understanding this intra-madhhab dispute sharpens your ability to weigh transmitted opinions and follow the tarjih process.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding when Zuhr time ends. The first says it ends when the shadow is twice the object's height (excluding midday shadow). The second says it ends when the shadow equals the object's height.
The second narration is also the view of the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Within the Hanafi school, the opponent is the second narration itself, supported by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Their view is that Zuhr ends when the shadow equals the object's height (excluding midday shadow).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani cited the hadith of Abu Huraira: 'Pray Zuhr when your shadow is like you, and Asr when your shadow is twice you.' He argued that 'when your shadow is like you' indicates that Zuhr time ends when the shadow equals the object.
The hadith is from Muwatta' Malik, transmitted as ahad.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator rejects this argument as weak (ليس بجيد) because the hadith does not explicitly define the end of Zuhr; it only commands when to pray Zuhr, not when its time expires. The preferred view relies on other evidence and the consensus of many Hanafi authorities.
The tarjih is supported by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Ghiyathiyyah, al-Bada'i', and al-Muhit.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the first narration, Zuhr time ends later (when shadow is twice the object). Under the second narration, Zuhr time ends earlier (when shadow equals the object). This affects how much time one has to pray Zuhr before Asr begins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وآخره إذا صارَ ظِلُّ المقياس مثلي المقياس سوى في الزَّوال مثلاً ، إذا كان فيء الزوال مقدار ربع المقياس ، فآخرُ وقت الظهر أن يصير ظله مثلى المقياس وربعه هذا في رواية عن أبي حنيفة . وفي روايةٍ أخرى عنه، وهو قول أبي يوسف ومحمد والشَّافِعِي : إذا صار ظل كلِّ شيءٍ مثله سوى فَيءِ الزَّوال. قوله : هذا ؛ أي خروج وقت الظهر عند صيرورة الظل مثلي المقياس ، رواية عن أبي حنيفة الا الله ، وهو الذي رجحه صاحب البحر الرائق في رسالة مستقلة له ، وقال في «الغياثية»: هو المختار ، وقال في «البدائع» و «المحيط»: هو الصحيح، وهو الذي اختاره أكثر أرباب المتون، واستدلَّ الإمامُ محمّدٌ في «الموطأ» بقول أبي هريرة : صل الظهر إذا كان ظلك مثلك، والعصر إذا كان ظلك مثليك، وهو استدلال ليس بجيد كما بيناه في «التعليق الممجد».
And its end: when the shadow of the measuring rod becomes twice the measuring rod, excluding the midday shadow, for example, if the midday shadow is a quarter of the measuring rod, then the end of Zuhr time is when its shadow becomes twice the measuring rod and its quarter. This is a narration from Abu Hanifa. And in another narration from him, which is the statement of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i: when the shadow of everything becomes equal to itself, excluding the midday shadow. His saying: "This" means the exit of Zuhr time when the shadow becomes twice the measuring rod is a narration from Abu Hanifa — may Allah have mercy on him — and it is the one favored by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq in an independent treatise, and he said in al-Ghiyathiyyah: it is the chosen one, and he said in al-Bada'i' and al-Muhit: it is the correct one, and it is the one chosen by most of the authors of the matn works. And Imam Muhammad argued in al-Muwatta' with the saying of Abu Huraira: "Pray Zuhr when your shadow is like you, and Asr when your shadow is twice you," but this argument is not good, as we have clarified in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the end time of Zuhr prayer. The author first defines the end of Zuhr as when the shadow of a measuring rod becomes twice its length, excluding the midday shadow (fay' al-zawal). He gives an example: if the midday shadow is a quarter of the rod's length, then Zuhr ends when the total shadow equals two and a quarter times the rod. He then reports that this definition is one narration from Abu Hanifa. However, there is another narration from Abu Hanifa, which is also the view of the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and of Imam al-Shafi'i, that Zuhr ends when the shadow of any object becomes equal to its own height (excluding the midday shadow). The commentator explains that the first narration (double the height) is the one favored by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, by al-Ghiyathiyyah, by al-Bada'i', by al-Muhit, and by most authors of matn works. He then notes that Imam Muhammad attempted to prove the second narration (equal height) by citing the hadith of Abu Huraira which says 'Pray Zuhr when your shadow is like you, and Asr when your shadow is twice you.' The commentator, however, rejects this argument as weak, indicating that the hadith is not decisive for this issue.

Key Terms
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawal): The minimal shadow that remains when the sun is at its zenith (midday).
مثلي المقياس (mithlay al-miqyas): Twice the length of the measuring rod (the object whose shadow is measured).
رواية (riwaya): A transmission of a legal opinion attributed to a mujtahid imam, here referring to two different opinions from Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred narration from Abu Hanifa, when does Zuhr time end?
A) When the shadow of an object becomes equal to its height, excluding the midday shadow.
B) When the shadow of an object becomes twice its height, excluding the midday shadow.
C) When the shadow disappears entirely.
D) When the shadow becomes three times the object's height.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two narrations on the end of Zuhr; the relied-upon position is that Zuhr ends when the shadow of an object is twice its height (excluding the midday shadow).

End of Zuhr Time: The Shadow Length Dispute
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on Zuhr/Asr timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi positions on the end of Zuhr time and state the mufta bihi, citing the evidence and tarjih authority.

Core Idea
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that Zuhr ends when the shadow equals the object, not when it doubles.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when exactly does Zuhr time end and Asr begin? The answer depends on how you measure the shadow. We'll unpack the three narrations from Abu Hanifa and the position of the Sahibayn, and see how later Hanafi masters settled on the equality view.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the core question: what shadow length marks the end of Zuhr and beginning of Asr? The dispute is about whether equality or doubling is the marker.
The noon shadow (fay' al-zawal) is always excluded from the calculation.
2
Enumerate the three Hanafi positions
List the three views: (1) Zuhr ends when shadow equals (Sahibayn and one narration from Abu Hanifa), (2) Zuhr ends when shadow doubles (another narration from Abu Hanifa), (3) Zuhr ends at equality, Asr begins at doubling (gap view, considered weak).
The gap view creates an interval with no required prayer, which is impermissible (la yu'ba' bih).
3
Examine the evidence for each view
The equality view relies on the hadith of Jabir and Jibril's demonstration. The doubling view relies on the hadith of Abu Hurairah, which the commentator criticizes as weak. Note that Imam Muhammad used that hadith but the commentator dismisses it.
The commentator mentions that most sound hadith support equality.
4
Follow the tarjih process
Later scholars like al-Tahawi, author of Ghurar al-Adhkar, al-Burhan, and al-Kurki preferred the equality view. The commentator endorses this and states that fatwa is given accordingly.
Tarjih is based on the strength of hadith and the practice of Jibril.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its consequence
The operative ruling is that Zuhr ends and Asr begins when the shadow equals the object (excluding noon shadow). This shortens Zuhr time compared to the doubling view and aligns with the Shafi'i school.
The thamarah al-khilaf: using equality makes Asr start earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة/ أوقات الصلاة

هذا في رواية عن أبي حنيفة وفي روايةٍ أخرى عنه، وهو قول أبي يوسف ومحمد والشَّافِعِي : إذا صار ظل كلِّ شيءٍ مثله سوى فَيءِ الزَّوال. فإذا أخذ الظل في الزيادةِ عُلِمَ أنها زالت فيخطّ على رأس الزيادة، فيكون من رأس الخط إلى العود فيء الزوال، فإذا صارَ  َظلُّ العودِ مثليه من رأس الخط لا من العود، خرج الظهر عنده. انتهى وفي «شرح مختصر الوقاية» لإلياس زاده: «ثمّ يُعَلِّم على رأس الظل علامة عند انحرافه، فإذا صار الظلّ من تلك العلامة لا من العامود مثل العامود خرج وقت الظهر عند أبي حنيفة ». انتهى [١]قوله : هذا؛ أي خروج وقت الظهر عند صيرورة الظل مثلي المقياس، رواية عن أبي حنيفة، وهو الذي رجحه صاحب البحر الرائق في رسالة مستقلة له، وقال في «الغياثية»: هو المختار، وقال في «البدائع» و «المحيط»: هو الصحيح، وهو الذي اختاره أكثر أرباب المتون، واستدلَّ الإمامُ محمّدٌ في «الموطأ» بقول أبي هريرة : صل الظهر إذا كان ظلك مثلك، والعصر إذا كان ظلك مثليك، وهو استدلال ليس بجيد كما بيناه في «التعليق الممجد».

وللعصر منه إلى غيبتها فوقتُ العصر من آخر وقت الظهر على القولين وروى عن أبي حنيفة أنه بالمثل يخرجُ الظهر، وبالمثلين يدخل العصر، فما بينهما وقت مهمل وهو قول لا يعبأ به، وأكثر الأحاديث الصحيحة دالة على أنّ بالمثل يخرجُ الظهر ويدخلُ العصر، فمن ثمّ قال الطحاوي : وبه نأخذ، وقال في «غرر الأذكار» : هو المأخوذ به، وفي «البرهان» : هو الأظهر ؛ لبيان جبريل، وفي «فيض الكركي»: عليه عمل الناس اليوم، وبه يفتى، وفي المقام تفصيل ليس هذا موضعه.
Book of Prayer / Prayer Times
This is in one narration from Abu Hanifa. And in another narration from him, and it is the saying of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i: when the shadow of everything becomes equal to it except the midday shadow. So when the shadow begins to increase, it is known that the sun has declined, so he draws a line at the head of the increase. Thus from the head of the line to the stick is the midday shadow. Then when the shadow of the stick becomes twice from the head of the line, not from the stick, Zuhr time exits according to him. End. And in 'Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah' by Ilyas Zada: 'Then he marks at the head of the shadow a marker at its decline. Then when the shadow from that marker, not from the pillar, becomes equal to the pillar, the time of Zuhr exits according to Abu Hanifa.' End. [1] His saying: 'this' means the exit of Zuhr time when the shadow becomes twice the measure, a narration from Abu Hanifa, and it is the one preferred by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq in an independent treatise of his. And he said in al-Ghiyathiyya: it is the chosen one. And he said in al-Bada'i' and al-Muhit: it is the correct one. And it is the one chosen by most authors of texts. Imam Muhammad argued in al-Muwatta' with the saying of Abu Hurairah: 'Pray Zuhr when your shadow is like you, and Asr when your shadow is twice you.' And this argument is not good, as we explained in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad.

And for Asr, from its [Zuhr's] end to sunset, so the time of Asr is from the last of Zuhr time according to the two sayings. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that with equality Zuhr exits, and with doubling Asr enters, and between them is a wasted time, and this is a saying not to be regarded. And most sound hadith indicate that with equality Zuhr exits and Asr enters. Hence al-Tahawi said: we take this. And he said in 'Ghurar al-Adhkar': it is the adopted. And in 'al-Burhan': it is the most apparent, due to Jibril's demonstration. And in 'Fayd al-Kurki': upon it is the practice of people today, and it is given as fatwa. And in this place is a detail not appropriate here.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute, also involving al-Shafi'i, regarding the end of Zuhr prayer time and the beginning of Asr. The core issue is the shadow length that marks the exit of Zuhr and entry of Asr. Abu Hanifa has multiple narrations: one states that Zuhr exits when the shadow becomes twice the height of the object (excluding the noon shadow), which is the view preferred by some later Hanafi scholars like the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and most text authors. Another narration from Abu Hanifa, which is also the view of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and al-Shafi'i, states that Zuhr exits when the shadow becomes equal to the object (excluding the noon shadow). A third narration from Abu Hanifa posits a gap: Zuhr exits at equality and Asr enters at doubling, leaving a time between. The commentator notes that the sound hadith (like the hadith of Jabir) support the equality view, and hence later scholars like al-Tahawi, the author of Ghurar al-Adhkar, and al-Burhan adopt this position. The fatwa today is upon the equality view. The hadith used by Imam Muhammad from Abu Hurairah is criticized as being weak evidence. This passage thus clarifies the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ظل (zill): Shadow cast by an object due to sunlight.
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawal): The residual shadow at the moment of sun's zenith (declination).
مثل (mithl): Equality of shadow length to object height.
مثلي (mithlay): Twice the shadow length of the object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zuhr ends when shadow is twice the object, and Asr begins when shadow is triple.
B) Zuhr ends when shadow equals the object, and Asr begins at that same moment.
C) Zuhr ends when shadow equals the object, and Asr begins when shadow is twice.
D) Zuhr ends at sunset, and Asr begins one hour later.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi for the end of Zuhr and beginning of Asr is when the shadow of an object (excluding noon shadow) equals its height.

Time of Asr Prayer and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute over Asr start time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the beginning of Asr time and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The beginning of Asr is disputed: Abu Hanifa says at double shadow, the Sahibayn at equal; fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah delves into the precise moment when Asr prayer time begins. While the end of Asr is unanimously sunset, the start has a significant intra-madhhab difference. The author presents the views of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, then shows how later Hanafi authorities settled on the position of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
State the common ground
Both sides agree that the end of Asr time is sunset, based on the hadith about catching a rak'ah before sunset.
This is not contested.
2
Identify the dispute
The beginning of Asr: Abu Hanifa holds it begins when shadow is double the object's height; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it begins when shadow equals the object's height.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa cited the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet prayed Asr when shadows were double. However, the commentator argues this does not prove Asr cannot be prayed earlier.
Hadith is authentic, but its implication is not exclusive.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn cited another hadith of Jabir where the Prophet prayed Asr when shadows were equal. This is more direct evidence for the beginning time.
This hadith is also authentic and appears in Sunan al-Nasa'i.
5
Determine the tarjih
Later authorities like al-Tahawi, al-Burhan, and al-Kurki preferred the Sahibayn's view. The practice of the people and fatwa today follow this view, as it is supported by more explicit hadith.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللعصر منه إلى غيبتها فوقتُ العصر من آخر وقت الظهر على القولين" وروى عن أبي حنيفة أنه بالمثل يخرجُ الظهر، وبالمثلين يدخل العصر، فما بينهما وقت مهمل وهو قول لا يعبأ به، وأكثر الأحاديث الصحيحة دالة على أنّ بالمثل يخرجُ الظهر ويدخلُ العصر، فمن ثمّ قال الطحاوي: وبه نأخذ، وقال في «غرر الأذكار»: هو المأخوذ به، وفي «البرهان»: هو الأظهر لبيان جبريل، وفي «فيض الكركي»: عليه عمل الناس اليوم وبه يفتى، وفي المقام تفصيل ليس هذا موضعه، مَن شاء الاطلاع عليه فليرجع إلى «السعاية». (1) قوله: على القولين؛ أي قول أبي حنيفة وقول الصاحبين له في الابتداء حديث جابر: «صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حين صار ظل كل شيء مثليه» أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة بسند لا بأس به، وفيه أنه لا دلالة له على أنه لا يدخل وقت العصر قبله. ولهما حديث جابر المروي في سنن النسائي وغيره: «إنه صلى العصر حين صار ظل كل شيء مثله». ولهم في الانتهاء حديث: «مَن أدرك ركعة قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر» على ما سيأتي ذكره عن قريب إن شاء الله، فإنه يدل على أن غروب الشمس منتهى وقته، وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة شاهدة عليه. (1) لكن استحسن صاحب رد المحتار (1 : 240) أن الاحتياط أن لا يؤخر الظهر إلى المثل، وأن لا يصلي العصر حتى يبلغ المثلين؛ ليكون مؤدياً للصلاتين في وقتهما بالإجماع. وينظر «فتح القدير» (1 : 193) (2) في «مختصره» (ص 23). (5) في صحيح البخاري (1: 204) وصحيح مسلم (1: 424) وغيرهما.
And for Asr, from it until sunset. The time of Asr is from the end of Zuhr time according to the two opinions. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that with the equal (shadow) Zuhr exits and with the double Asr enters, so between them is an ignored time, which is a saying not to be considered. And most of the authentic hadiths indicate that with the equal Zuhr exits and Asr enters, hence al-Tahawi said: we adopt this. And he said in 'Ghurar al-Adhkar': it is the adopted view, and in 'al-Burhan': it is the most apparent due to the explanation of Jibril, and in 'Fayd al-Kurki': upon it are the people today and with it fatwa is given. (1) His saying: according to the two opinions; meaning the saying of Abu Hanifa and the saying of the two companions. Regarding the beginning, the hadith of Jabir: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed with us when the shadow of everything became double', narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba with a chain not objectionable, and in it there is no evidence that Asr time does not enter before it. And for them is the hadith of Jabir in Sunan al-Nasa'i etc.: 'He prayed Asr when the shadow of everything became equal.' And for them regarding the ending, the hadith: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah before the sun sets has caught Asr' as will be mentioned shortly, for it indicates that sunset is the end of its time, and in this chapter many reports witness to it. (1) But the author of Radd al-Muhtar considered it cautious not to delay Zuhr to the equal, and not to pray Asr until after the double has been reached, to be performing both prayers in their times by consensus. And look at Fath al-Qadir (1:193) (2) in his Mukhtasar (p.23). (3) And al-Shurunbulali supported it in his Hashiya on al-Durar (1:51), and the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar chose it (p.240). (4) With the wording: from Jabir said: 'A man asked the Messenger of Allah about the times of prayer, so he said: Pray with me, so he prayed Zuhr when the sun declined, Asr when the shadow of everything was equal...' in Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra (1:469) and al-Mujtaba (1:251) etc. (5) In Sahih al-Bukhari (1:204) and Sahih Muslim (1:424) etc.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the base matn regarding the time of Asr prayer. The base text states that Asr time extends from the end of Zuhr time until sunset. The commentator then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the beginning of Asr. According to Abu Hanifa, Zuhr exits when the shadow of an object equals its height, and Asr enters when the shadow is double, leaving a gap in between. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that Asr enters immediately after Zuhr when the shadow equals the object's height. The commentator notes that most authentic hadiths support the view of the two companions, and this is the adopted view of later scholars like al-Tahawi, al-Burhan, and al-Kurki, and it is the basis for fatwa today. The footnotes elaborate: Abu Hanifa's proof is the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet prayed Asr when shadows were double, but the commentator argues this does not preclude entry earlier. The Sahibayn's proof is the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet prayed Asr when shadows were equal. The ending time for Asr is sunset, as per the hadith about catching a rak'ah before sunset. The commentator adds that some scholars recommend caution: not to delay Zuhr to the equal shadow nor pray Asr before the double, to ensure performing both prayers within their agreed times.

Key Terms
المثل (al-mithl): The length of the shadow of an object equal to its height after zawal, excluding the fay' al-zawal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When the shadow of an object equals its height
C) When the sun declines from its zenith
D) When the shadow returns after midday

Key Takeaway
The start of Asr in the Hanafi school is when the shadow equals the object, according to the mufta bihi view of the Sahibayn.

Time of Maghrib Prayer and Definition of Shafaq
Defines ending time of Maghrib and identifies shafaq as redness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time of Maghrib prayer, define shafaq according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, and apply the criteria for sunset in different environments.

Core Idea
Maghrib ends when the redness (shafaq) disappears; fatwa is on the Sahibayn's definition.

This lesson examines a commentary passage that clarifies the end time of Maghrib prayer by defining a key term: shafaq (twilight). While the base text mentions the time until the disappearance of shafaq, the commentator specifies that the relied-upon Hanafi position identifies shafaq as the redness after sunset. Understanding this definition is essential for correctly determining Maghrib and Isha prayer times, especially during twilight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and the key term
The base text states that Maghrib time is from sunset until the disappearance of shafaq. The term shafaq is ambiguous, so the commentator explains it. Note that the prayer itself is fard ayn.
Shafaq is later defined.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
The commentator cites the hadith of Muslim: 'The time of Maghrib prayer is as long as the shafaq has not set.' This is the primary dalil. The term shafaq appears without qualification, requiring interpretation.
Thubut is zanni; dalala is also zanni.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute and tarjih
Abu Hanifa held shafaq is whiteness, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held it is redness. The commentator states that fatwa is given on the Sahibayn's view. Identify the evidence for each and the reason for choosing the Sahibayn's view.
The mawquf narration from Ibn Umar is a key evidence for redness.
4
Understand the practical application for sunset determination
Shaykh al-Islam al-Taftazani clarifies that sunset is the disappearance of the sun's disk. In open areas, this is directly observable; in built-up areas or mountains, it is determined by the absence of sunlight on structures and the approach of darkness from the east.
The same criterion applies for breaking the fast in Ramadan.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The difference between redness and whiteness affects the end of Maghrib and beginning of Isha. If shafaq is redness, Isha begins earlier; if whiteness, Maghrib lasts longer. The mufta bihi view shortens Maghrib time.
In practice, using the Sahibayn's view aligns with common fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمغرب منه إلى مغيب الشفق، وهو الحمرة عندهما، وبه يُفْتَى. [1] قوله: إلى أن تغيب الشمس؛ قال شيخ الإسلام التفتازاني: المعتبر في غروب الشمس سقوط قرص الشمس، وهذا ظاهر في الصحراء، وأما في البنيان وقلل الجبال فبأن لا يرى شيء من شعاعها على أطراف البنيان وقلل الجبال، وأن يقبل الظلام من المشرق. [2] قوله: إلى مغيب الشفق؛ بفتحتين؛ لحديث مسلم مرفوعاً: «وقت صلاة المغرب ما لم يغب الشفق»، وفي رواية له: «وقت المغرب إذا غابت الشمس ما لم يسقط الشفق». [3] قوله: وهو الحمرة؛ كما أخرجه الدارقطني والبيهقي وغيرهما عن ابن عمر موقوفاً، وروي مرفوعاً أيضاً، وسنده ضعيف. (1) قال: إذا أقبل الليل من ها هنا وأدبر النهار من ها هنا وغربت الشمس فقد أفطر الصائم. في صحيح البخاري (2: 691) وصحيح مسلم (2: 772). قال العلامة الحصكفي في الدر المنتقى (2: 230): «أي إذا وجد الظلمة حساً في جهته فقد دخل وقت الفطر أو صار مقطراً». قال الحافظ ابن حجر في فتح الباري (2: 42): سقوط قرص الشمس يدخل به وقت المغرب، ولا يخفى أن محله ما إذا كان لا يحول بين رؤيتها غاربة وبين الرائي حائل: أي من جبل أو عمران أو غيرهما، وهذا إنما يتم في الصحراء لا في العمران كما في نيل الأوطار (2: 5-6) وغيره.
And for Maghrib, from it until the disappearance of the twilight (shafaq), and it is the redness according to them (the two companions), and with it fatwa is given. [1] His saying: until the sun sets; Shaykh al-Islam al-Taftazani said: The criterion for sunset is the disappearance of the sun's disk. This is apparent in the desert. As for built-up areas and mountain peaks, it is that no trace of its rays is seen on the edges of buildings and mountain peaks, and that darkness approaches from the east. [2] His saying: until the disappearance of shafaq; with two fat-has; due to the hadith of Muslim raised: 'The time of Maghrib prayer is as long as the shafaq has not set.' And in another narration: 'The time of Maghrib is when the sun sets as long as the shafaq has not fallen.' [3] His saying: it is the redness; as narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi and others from Ibn Umar as a stop (mawquf), and also narrated raised, but its chain is weak. (1) He said: When the night approaches from this direction and the day recedes from this direction and the sun has set, then the fasting person has broken his fast. In Sahih al-Bukhari (2:691) and Sahih Muslim (2:772). Al-Allama al-Haskafi said in al-Durr al-Muntaqa (2:230): 'i.e., when darkness is perceived in his direction, the time of breaking the fast has entered or he has become a breaking faster.' Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari (2:42): The setting of the sun's disk enters the time of Maghrib, and it does not hide that its place is when there is no barrier between the viewer and the sun setting, i.e., a mountain or buildings or other. This is only in the desert, not in built-up areas as in Nayl al-Awtar (2:5-6) and others.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the base matn regarding the time of Maghrib prayer. The base text states that Maghrib time runs from sunset until the disappearance of the shafaq (twilight), and specifies that according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), shafaq is the redness in the sky after sunset, and this is the view on which fatwa is given. The commentator then elaborates: The criterion for sunset is the actual disappearance of the sun's disk (qurs). This is straightforward in open deserts, but in built-up areas or mountainous regions, sunset is indicated by the absence of sunlight on high structures and the approach of darkness from the east. The hadith of Muslim is cited: 'The time of Maghrib is as long as the shafaq has not set.' The definition of shafaq as redness is supported by a mawquf narration from Ibn Umar (also marfu' but weak). The passage also connects this to the time of breaking the fast in Ramadan, citing the well-known hadith from Bukhari and Muslim about the approach of night and the setting of the sun. Al-Haskafi explains that when darkness is perceived, the fasting person has broken his fast. Ibn Hajar clarifies that the setting of the sun's disk is the criterion, provided there is no barrier to sight; otherwise, one relies on the absence of sunlight on buildings.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; specifically, the redness in the western horizon according to the two companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, what is the definition of shafaq?
A) The white twilight after sunset
B) The redness after sunset
C) The complete darkness after sunset
D) The orange glow before sunrise

Key Takeaway
Maghrib time ends when the redness (shafaq) disappears, not the whiteness, and fatwa is given on the Sahibayn's definition.

Salah — Prayer

Definition of Shafaq: Red or White Twilight?
Commentary on shafaq and its impact on prayer times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on shafaq and explain which is mufta bihi and why.

Core Idea
The definition of shafaq determines the end of Maghrib time; the Hanafi school relies on the red twilight (Sahibayn) for fatwa.

In this lesson, we explore a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the twilight after sunset. The definition of shafaq directly determines when Maghrib prayer time ends and Isha begins. The Imam and his two disciples differ, and the later school has settled on one view. Understanding this dispute clarifies how prayer times are fixed in Hanafi practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What exactly is shafaq? The term appears in hadith without specification. The dispute is whether it means the red twilight or the white twilight that follows.
2
Examine the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa holds that shafaq is the white twilight; the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is the red twilight. Identify who holds which view and note that the later school follows the disciples.
3
Review the evidence
The text cites the hadith of Muslim: 'Time of Maghrib is as long as the shafaq has not disappeared.' It also mentions a report from Ibn Umar defining shafaq as red, albeit with a weak chain. The disciples rely on the common understanding and companion practice.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its impact
The fatwa is given on the view of Sahibayn: shafaq is red. Therefore, Maghrib time ends when the red twilight vanishes. This earlier end time directly affects when Isha begins.
Practical consequence: In regions with long twilights, the difference can be significant.

[3] His saying: 'according to them'; he repeated it even though it is unnecessary due to the existence of the lam (preposition) on Isha and Witr for clarification and emphasis in removing the illusion that his saying 'until dawn' is attached only to Witr. As for the beginning of Isha, it is indicated by the hadith of the imamate of Jibril, when he led the Prophet, teaching him the beginnings of the times, with Isha prayer at the mere disappearance of the shafaq. As for its end, it is indicated by what was narrated by...
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the prayer times as laid out in the matn (base text) of al-Wiqaya. It focuses on the times of Maghrib, Isha, and Witr prayers, with a central dispute regarding the definition of shafaq (twilight). The passage first addresses Maghrib time, stating that it lasts from sunset until the disappearance of shafaq. The commentator clarifies that sunset is defined by the disk of the sun vanishing, which is straightforward in open desert but in built-up areas or mountains, it is when no rays remain on the tops of structures. Then the passage defines shafaq: according to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), shafaq is the red twilight, and this is the position upon which fatwa is given. Evidence is provided from a hadith in Sahih Muslim that the time for Maghrib extends until the shafaq disappears. Another hadith from al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi attributes the red definition to Ibn Umar, though as a mawquf (companion saying) with a weak marfu' version. The commentary also notes that al-Haskafi and others confirm this as the madhhab and the basis for fatwa, although Abu Hanifa's view (white twilight) is considered more precautionary. The passage then moves to Isha time: it begins at the end of Maghrib time, i.e., after the shafaq disappears. For Witr, according to the two disciples, its time is from after Isha until dawn, and it is a sunnah that is an accompaniment of Isha, supported by a hadith about Witr being better than red camels. In contrast, Abu Hanifa holds that Witr is an independent wajib (obligatory) prayer, and its time is essentially the same as Isha, but it must be delayed until after Isha due to the order of prayers. The practical difference emerges in cases where one prays Witr before Isha forgetfully or remembers that he prayed it without wudu: according to Abu Hanifa, it is not repeated, while according to the disciples, it must be repeated. The passage concludes with a grammatical note that the phrase 'until dawn' applies only to Witr, not to Isha, and that the beginning of Isha is established by the hadith of Jibril (Gabriel) leading the Prophet in prayer at the moment the shafaq disappears.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; its color is debated: red according to Sahibayn, white according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school's mufta bihi, what is shafaq?
A) Red twilight
B) White twilight
C) Darkness
D) Sunrise

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the red twilight (shafaq) as the end of Maghrib time, based on the view of the two disciples.

Status of Witr Prayer: Wajib or Sunnah?
Commentary on the status and timing of Witr prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the status of Witr and identify the mufta bihi and its practical consequences.

Core Idea
Witr is considered wajib by Abu Hanifa but sunnah by the two disciples; the relied-upon view is that it is a sunnah mu'akkada after Isha.

Witr prayer is an odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, but its legal status is debated within the Hanafi school. Is it an independent obligation or a emphasized sunnah? The answer affects whether one must make up missed Witr and how it interacts with Isha. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views
Abu Hanifa: Witr is wajib (obligatory) and independent; its time is the same as Isha but must be delayed after Isha. Sahibayn: Witr is sunnah mu'akkada (emphasized sunnah) and a dependent accompaniment of Isha, its time from after Isha to dawn.
2
Examine the evidence for each view
Sahibayn cite the hadith: 'Allah commanded you with a prayer better than red camels - Witr - between Isha and dawn.' This positions Witr as an optional but strongly recommended prayer. Abu Hanifa relies on general commands and the fact that it is obligatory (wajib) in his usul.
3
Analyze the practical consequence
The text gives a case: if one prays Witr before Isha forgetfully, according to Abu Hanifa the prayer is valid and no need to repeat; according to Sahibayn, Witr must be repeated because it must come after Isha.
Also, if one misses Witr, according to Abu Hanifa it must be made up; according to Sahibayn, it is recommended but not obligatory.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The text implies that the fatwa is on the view of Sahibayn, as the passage presents their view as the basis for timing and the practical examples align with their position. Later Hanafi works confirm that Witr is sunnah mu'akkada.

[3] His saying: 'and it is the redness' as al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi and others narrated from Ibn 'Umar as a mawquf, and also narrated as marfu' but its chain is weak. (1) He said: 'When the night comes from here and the day retreats from here and the sun has set, then the fasting person has broken his fast' in Sahih al-Bukhari (2: 691) and Sahih Muslim (2: 772). Al-Allama al-Haskafi said in al-Durr al-Muntaqa (2: 230): 'That is, when darkness is perceived in his direction, then the time for breaking the fast has entered or he has become a muftir.' Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari (2: 42): 'The setting of the disk of the sun enters the time of Maghrib, and it is not hidden that its place is when there is no barrier between seeing it setting and the viewer, i.e., a mountain or building or other than that, and this is only complete in the desert, not in built-up areas, as in Nayl al-Awtar (2: 5-6) and others.' (2) In Sahih Muslim (1: 427) and Musnad Ahmad (2: 210) and others. (3) In Sahih Muslim (1: 427) and others. He said in al-Nahr: 'The effect of the difference appears in the case where he offers Witr before it (Isha) forgetfully, or he remembers that he prayed it only without wudu; he does not repeat it according to him, and according to them he repeats it.' [3] His saying: 'according to them'; he repeated it even though it is unnecessary due to the existence of the lam (preposition) on Isha and Witr for clarification and emphasis in removing the illusion that his saying 'until dawn' is attached only to Witr. And the hadith indicating the time of Witr beginning and end has passed. As for the beginning of Isha, it is indicated by the hadith of the imamate of Jibril, when he led the Prophet, teaching him the beginnings of the times, with Isha prayer at the mere disappearance of the shafaq. Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the prayer times as laid out in the matn (base text) of al-Wiqaya. It focuses on the times of Maghrib, Isha, and Witr prayers, with a central dispute regarding the definition of shafaq (twilight). The passage first addresses Maghrib time, stating that it lasts from sunset until the disappearance of shafaq. The commentator clarifies that sunset is defined by the disk of the sun vanishing, which is straightforward in open desert but in built-up areas or mountains, it is when no rays remain on the tops of structures. Then the passage defines shafaq: according to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), shafaq is the red twilight, and this is the position upon which fatwa is given. Evidence is provided from a hadith in Sahih Muslim that the time for Maghrib extends until the shafaq disappears. Another hadith from al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi attributes the red definition to Ibn Umar, though as a mawquf (companion saying) with a weak marfu' version. The commentary also notes that al-Haskafi and others confirm this as the madhhab and the basis for fatwa, although Abu Hanifa's view (white twilight) is considered more precautionary. The passage then moves to Isha time: it begins at the end of Maghrib time, i.e., after the shafaq disappears. For Witr, according to the two disciples, its time is from after Isha until dawn, and it is a sunnah that is an accompaniment of Isha, supported by a hadith about Witr being better than red camels. In contrast, Abu Hanifa holds that Witr is an independent wajib (obligatory) prayer, and its time is essentially the same as Isha, but it must be delayed until after Isha due to the order of prayers. The practical difference emerges in cases where one prays Witr before Isha forgetfully or remembers that he prayed it without wudu: according to Abu Hanifa, it is not repeated, while according to the disciples, it must be repeated. The passage concludes with a grammatical note that the phrase 'until dawn' applies only to Witr, not to Isha, and that the beginning of Isha is established by the hadith of Jibril (Gabriel) leading the Prophet in prayer at the moment the shafaq disappears.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): A prayer with an odd number of rak'ahs performed after Isha; its status and timing are disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what is the status of Witr prayer?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah mu'akkada
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that Witr is a sunnah mu'akkada prayer, performed after Isha until dawn, and omission does not incur sin.

Shafaq Definition and Witr Status: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary defining shafaq and explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute on Witr's status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of shafaq and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the beginning time of Isha and the ruling of Witr, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf in the case of forgetfulness.

Core Idea
The definition of shafaq determines when Isha begins; whether Witr is wajib or sunnah changes the consequence of offering it before Isha.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah commentary on Al-Wiqayah discusses two connected disputes within the Hanafi school: the definition of shafaq (twilight) and the legal status of Witr. Abu Hanifa defines shafaq as the whiteness after the redness, while the Sahibayn define it as the redness itself. This affects when Isha begins. Additionally, Abu Hanifa considers Witr an independent wajib, while the Sahibayn consider it a sunnah dependent on Isha. The commentary shows how these differences lead to distinct practical outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
Recognize that the passage deals with two separate but linked disputes: (1) the definition of shafaq, and (2) the status of Witr. Note how the commentator connects them.
The opening sentence of the matn sets the time for Isha 'from it' (i.e., from the disappearance of shafaq) and for Witr 'after Isha until dawn' according to the Sahibayn.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his evidence
Abu Hanifa defines shafaq as the whiteness that remains after the redness disappears. He also holds that Witr is an independent obligation (wajib), distinct from Isha, with its own time that coincides with Isha's time but is delayed due to order. His evidence includes narrations from Abu Bakr, Mu'adh, and Aisha.
The commentator says 'وهو المروى عن أبي بكر ومعاذ وعائشة' – these sahaba transmitted the definition of shafaq as whiteness.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad define shafaq as the redness itself. They consider Witr a sunnah that follows Isha, with its time starting after Isha until dawn. Their primary evidence is the hadith: 'Indeed Allah commanded you with a prayer better than red camels, it is Witr; He made it for you between Isha prayer and dawn.'
The hadith is cited in the passage: 'إنّ الله أمركم بصلاة هي خير لكم من حُمُرِ النعم، وهي الوتر، جعلها الله لكم فيما بين صلاة العشاء إلى أن يطلع الفجر'.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference in shafaq definition means Isha begins at different times: according to the Sahibayn at redness disappearance, according to Abu Hanifa at whiteness disappearance. For Witr, if one prays Witr before Isha forgetfully, Abu Hanifa says it is valid (since Witr is independent and its time is the same as Isha), while the Sahibayn say it is invalid and must be repeated (since it depends on Isha and order).
The commentator quotes from 'al-Nahr': 'أثر الخلاف يظهر فيما إذا قدم الوتر عليها ناسياً... لا يعيده عنده، وعندهما يعيده'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Within the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa: shafaq is the whiteness, and Witr is wajib. Thus, the practical ruling follows Abu Hanifa's view.
Though the commentator does not explicitly tarjih here, later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Hidayah) adopt Abu Hanifa's positions.

Supporting it is the hadith: 'Indeed Allah commanded you with a prayer that is better for you than red camels, and it is Witr. Allah has appointed it for you between the Isha prayer and the dawn.' Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Al-Wiqayah regarding the times for Isha and Witr prayers. The matn states that the time for Isha extends from the disappearance of the shafaq (twilight) until dawn, and the time for Witr is from after Isha until dawn, according to both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Hanifa, however, defines shafaq as the whiteness that remains after the redness has disappeared. This difference leads to a practical difference: according to the two companions, Isha begins with the disappearance of the redness, while according to Abu Hanifa it begins with the disappearance of the whiteness. The commentary elaborates that the preferred practice for Zuhr is before the shadow lengthens, for Asr after it doubles, for Maghrib before the redness disappears, and for Isha after the whiteness disappears. The passage then addresses the status of Witr: according to the two companions, Witr is a sunnah that follows Isha, and its time ends at dawn, as per a hadith. According to Abu Hanifa, Witr is an independent obligatory prayer (wajib), its time is the same as Isha, but due to the order of prayers, it is delayed to be performed after Isha. The practical effect of this ikhtilaf: if one prays Witr before Isha forgetfully, or remembers that he prayed Witr without wudu, according to Abu Hanifa he does not need to repeat it, whereas according to the two companions he must repeat it. The commentator also clarifies that the phrase 'to dawn' applies to both Isha and Witr, not just Witr, emphasizing that Isha's time also ends at dawn. The beginning of Isha time is indicated by the hadith of Jibril, when he led the Prophet at the time of the disappearance of the shafaq. The end of Isha time is indicated by a narration from Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Pray Isha during the night.' This commentary demonstrates the Hanafi method of reconciling hadith and the ikhtilaf within the school.

Key Terms
الشفق (ash-shafaq): Twilight after sunset; according to Abu Hanifa, the white glow after the redness, while according to the two companions, it is the redness itself.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha; Abu Hanifa considers it wajib, while the two companions consider it sunnah mu'akkadah.
الترتيب (at-tartib): Order between prayers; here it refers to the requirement to pray Isha before Witr. Dispute exists on whether it is a condition of validity or a recommended order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The Witr is invalid and must be repeated.

C) The Witr is valid but must be repeated after Isha.
D) The Isha prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The definition of shafaq and the status of Witr as an independent wajib are matters of legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, with Abu Hanifa's positions being mufta bihi.

Recommended Time for Fajr Prayer and Repetition for Invalid Wudu
Commentary on Fajr time recommendation and wudu repetition ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for Fajr prayer (isfar) and identify when a prayer must be repeated due to invalid wudu.

Core Idea
Start Fajr in light to recite 40-60 verses; if wudu was invalid, repeat the prayer.

This lesson unpacks two rulings from the Hanafi tradition for Fajr prayer: the sunnah of starting when there is enough light to recite with full care, and the fard obligation to repeat if wudu was later discovered invalid. The commentary reconciles different reports and shows that both practices have roots in the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the matn
Read the matn: it recommends starting Fajr in isfar and repeating if wudu becomes apparent invalid. These are two separate rulings: one about timing, one about validity.
2
Define isfar and its significance
Isfar is when the dawn light spreads. The recommended start is when one can recite 40-60 verses with tartil, which ensures proper recitation.
Taghlis (darkness) is also allowed, but isfar is preferred unless the imam recites long passages.
3
Understand the consequence of invalid wudu
The matn says 'then repeat it if the invalidity of his wudu becomes apparent.' This is because wudu is a condition (shart) for prayer; if it was broken, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This applies regardless of intention.
4
Note the intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab perspectives
Some Hanafi scholars (like al-Tahawi) preferred taghlis if reciting long, but the relied-upon view is isfar. The Shafi'i school prefers taghlis. The commentator reconciles by noting that long recitation can make taghlis equivalent to isfar in finish time.
The practical difference: a Hanafi imam who recites long may start earlier; one who recites short should start later.
