(٢) قوله : بحيث يمكنه ؛ تحديد للإسفار المستحب؛ أي في وقت يمكنه أن يقرأ فيها مع الترتيل وإعطاء الحروف والكلمات القرآنية حقها بقدر أربعين آية إلى ستين كما هو (۱) في «شرح معاني الآثار (۱) : (۱۵۹) وقال الطحاوي: ففي هذا أنه جعل الليل كله وقتا لها على أنه لا يغفلها فوجه ذلك عندنا على أن تركه إياها إلى نصف الليل إغفال لها وتركه إياها إلى أن يمضي ثلث الليل ليس بإغفال لها (۲) (الحجة على أهل المدينة» (۱) : (۱) : وفيه : قال محمد بن الحسن الله قد جاء في ذلك آثار مختلفة من التغليس والإسفار بالفجر، والإسفار بالفجر أحب الينا ؛ لأن القوم كانوا يغلسون فيطيلون القراءة فينصرفون كما ينصرف أصحاب الإسفار ويدرك النائم وغيره الصلاة، وقد بلغنا عن أبي بكر الصديق الله أنه قرأ سورة البقرة في صلاة الصبح فإنما كانوا يغلسون لذلك فأما من خفف وصلى بسورة المفصل ونحوها فإنه ينبغي له أن يسفر، وقد بلغنا أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر». (۳) لكن عن إبراهيم النخعي الله قال : «ما اجتمع أصحاب رسول الله له على شيء ما اجتمعوا على التنوير» في مصنف ابن أبي شيبة» (۱): (٢٨٤) ، و«الآثار» (۱ : ۲۰ ، ۵۰)، و«شرح . قال معاني الآثار» (١) : ١٨٤) ، قال الزيلعي في نصب الراية (۱) : ۲۳۹): سنده صحیح قـ الإمام الطحاوي في شرح معاني الآثار (۱): ١٨٤) : ولا يصح أن يجتمعوا على خلاف ما كان رسول الله .
It is recommended for Fajr to start in the light (musfiran) such that one can recite forty verses or more with tartil, and then to repeat it if the invalidity of his wudu becomes apparent. (It is recommended for Fajr to start in the light such that one can recite forty verses or more, then to repeat it if the invalidity of his wudu becomes apparent. Al-Tahawi narrated from Umar that he wrote to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Pray Isha during the night.') [1] His saying: 'the start': he indicated by it that what is recommended is to start the Fajr prayer and finish it both during isfar - i.e., the time when light appears and whiteness spreads. Al-Tahawi and others chose the recommendation of starting in ghalas (darkness) and finishing during isfar by prolonging the recitation. This is what Imam Muhammad explicitly stated in his book al-Hujaj, and by this most of the hadiths on the chapter of isfar and the chapter of taghlis are reconciled, as we explained in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' Muhammad. [2] His saying: 'such that he can': a specification of the recommended isfar; i.e., at a time when he can recite with tartil, giving the letters and Quranic words their due, to the extent of forty to sixty verses, as is (1) In Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (1:159), al-Tahawi said: In this, he made the whole night a time for it, but not delaying it; its interpretation according to us is that leaving it until half the night is negligence, and leaving it until one third of the night passes is not negligence. (2) Al-Hujja 'ala Ahl al-Madina (1:1): It contains: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan said: There have come various reports on taghlis and isfar for Fajr. Isfar for Fajr is more beloved to us because the people used to pray in darkness but prolonged the recitation, so they finished at the same time as those who pray in light, and the sleeping one and others catch the prayer. It has reached us that Abu Bakr al-Siddiq recited Surah al-Baqarah in Fajr prayer, and they only prayed in darkness for that reason. As for one who shortens and prays short surahs, he should pray in light. It has reached us that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Make isfar with Fajr, for it is greater in reward.' (3) But from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'The companions of the Messenger of Allah did not agree on anything as they agreed on al-tanwir (lightening).' In Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba (1:284), al-Athar (1:20,50), Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (1:184), al-Zayla'i said in Nasb al-Raya (1:239): its chain is authentic. Imam al-Tahawi said in Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (1:184): It is not possible that they agreed on something contrary to what the Messenger of Allah did.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn stating the recommendation for Fajr prayer. The matn says: 'It is recommended for Fajr to start in the light (musfiran) such that one can recite forty or more verses with tartil, and then to repeat it if the invalidity of one's wudu becomes apparent.' The commentator explains that the recommendation is to begin and end the Fajr prayer in isfar, which is when light spreads and whiteness appears. However, there is a difference: some scholars like al-Tahawi preferred starting in ghalas (darkness) and finishing in isfar by prolonging the recitation. Imam Muhammad stated in his book al-Hujaj that isfar is more beloved because the earlier companions used to pray in darkness but recited long passages, so they finished at the same time as those who started later. For those who recite short surahs, they should start in isfar. The hadith 'Make isfar with Fajr, for it is greater in reward' supports this. Yet, there is also a report from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the companions agreed on al-tanwir (praying at the time when there is light), which indicates the practice of starting in light. The commentator reconciles the various hadith by stating that the recommendation accommodates both practices: if one recites long, he may start earlier; if short, he starts later. The second part of the matn mentions that if one later finds out his wudu was invalid, he must repeat the prayer. This is a straightforward ruling: the validity of prayer depends on wudu; if it is discovered later, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Terms
الإسفار (al-isar): The time when light appears and whiteness spreads at dawn, making it possible to clearly see.
التغليس (at-taghlis): Praying in the early dawn when it is still dark.
الترتيل (at-tartil): Reciting the Quran slowly and clearly, giving each letter its due and observing the rules of tajweed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what is one recommended to do if he later discovers his wudu was invalid during Fajr prayer?
A) He does not need to repeat as it was unintentional.
B) He should repeat the prayer because wudu is a condition of validity.
C) He should only make up the wudu for future prayers.
D) He should give charity as expiation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends starting Fajr in isfar for proper recitation, but wudu validity is a non-negotiable condition; if broken, the prayer must be repeated.

The Time for Fajr: Isfar vs. Taghlis – Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling with proof and exceptions for Fajr time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for Fajr prayer for men and women, identify the proof from the hadith, and apply the exceptions for Muzdalifah and women.

Core Idea
The command 'asfiru' indicates recommendation due to reward, not obligation; taghlis is for women and Muzdalifah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the Hanafi ruling on the preferred time for Fajr prayer. While the Prophet's verbal command 'Pray Fajr in brightness' seems obligatory, the attached reason of greater reward reduces it to a recommendation. The author also clarifies exceptions: for women and for Fajr at Muzdalifah during Hajj, praying in darkness (taghlis) is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act ruled upon? The prayer time. The text says 'yustahabb' (it is recommended).
The hukm level is mustahabb, not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith 'Asfiru bi'l-fajr fa-innahu a'zam li'l-ajr'.
This is a verbal hadith (qawl).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The imperative 'asfiru' would indicate wujub, but the attached clause 'fa-innahu a'zam li'l-ajr' diverts to istihbab.
Hanafi usul: an imperative with an attached reason indicates recommendation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
What is the Shafi'i position? They interpret the hadith as praying at true dawn, not brightness, and rely on the Prophet's action of taghlis.
The author rejects this interpretation based on the apparent wording.
5
Identify the exceptions
Who are the exceptions? Women and pilgrims at Muzdalifah should use taghlis.
For women, darkness is more concealing; for Muzdalifah, the Prophet prayed in darkness.

Book of Prayer / Times of Prayer 17. It is recommended for Fajr to begin in a state of [slight] brightness such that one can recite forty verses with tartil, or more, then repeat it if his ablution turned out to be invalid. [Text] It is recommended for Fajr to begin in a state of brightness such that one can recite forty verses with tartil, or more, then repeat it if his ablution turned out to be invalid. Al-Tahawi from 'Umar ? that he wrote to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Pray 'Isha until the night.' [1] His saying: 'the beginning'; He indicated by this that the recommended [act] is to begin the Fajr prayer and conclude both [the recitation?] in isfar – i.e., the time of light appearing and whiteness spreading. Al-Tahawi and others chose the recommendation of beginning in darkness (ghalas) and concluding in isfar by lengthening the recitation. This is what Imam Muhammad declared in his book al-Hujaj, and by this most of the ahadith reported in the chapter of isfar and the chapter of taghlis are reconciled, as we explained in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' Muhammad. (2) His saying: 'such that he can'; a specification of the recommended isfar: i.e., at a time when he can recite with tartil and giving the letters and words of the Qur'an their due, about forty to sixty verses, as is recommended therein. Then the repetition of Fajr prayer with purity and with the mentioned tartil if his prayer becomes invalid due to an invalidity in it or in its purity, all of that before sunrise. For if he prayed in very great brightness then his prayer turned out invalid due to forgetting the bath for janabah or ablution or other than that, his repetition would not be within the time. And all of this is for men who are not pilgrims praying in Muzdalifah, for Fajr of Muzdalifah is excepted from this, because isfar is not recommended for it but rather taghlis. Reports have come that he (sAws) prayed it there in darkness; al-Bukhari and others narrated it. It is mentioned in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others that for a woman, taghlis is recommended absolutely, because darkness is more concealing for her. [1] His saying: 'he said'; this hadith was narrated by al-Bazzar, al-Tahawi, al-Tabarani, Ibn Majah, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i and others through various chains with similar wordings. The apparent command in it, although it indicates obligation, but what follows it – i.e., His saying: 'for it is greater in reward' – turns it from obligation to recommendation. And since this hadith is a verbal [proof], it is given preponderance over what the authors of the Sahihs narrated 'that he prayed Fajr in darkness', because speech (qawl) is given precedence over action (fi'l), as is established in the books of usul. And the interpretation that what is meant by it is: pray at the appearance of true dawn and certainty of it, not before it, nor at a time of doubt between its appearance and non-appearance, as is transmitted from the Shafi'is, is refuted by the apparent wording of the hadith.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on the ruling regarding the preferred time for the Fajr prayer. The passage type is a ruling with proof (hukm ma'a dalil). The author begins by stating the ruling: it is mustahabb (recommended) to begin Fajr when there is enough light (isfar) to recite forty verses or more with proper tartil (measured recitation). If after praying one discovers that one's wudu was invalid, one may repeat the prayer as long as it is before sunrise. The author then explains the key terms: 'al-bidaya' (beginning) refers to starting the prayer in isfar, though some scholars like al-Tahawi and Imam Muhammad prefer to begin in darkness (ghalas) and finish in isfar by reciting longer passages, which reconciles the various ahadith. The specification 'such that he can' means the recommended isfar is when one can recite forty to sixty verses with tartil. The exception for repeating the prayer applies only if the deficiency is discovered before sunrise; if one prayed in extreme brightness and then discovered the invalidity, the repeat is not in time. All this applies to men who are not praying in Muzdalifah during Hajj, because for Fajr at Muzdalifah, taghlis is recommended as the Prophet did so. For women, taghlis is recommended in all cases for modesty. The author then discusses the hadith 'Asfiru bi'l-fajr' (Perform Fajr in brightness), which is a verbal command. Although the imperative form normally indicates obligation (wujub), the attached phrase 'for it is greater in reward' (fa-innahu a'zam li'l-ajr) diverts it to recommendation (istihbab). This hadith, being a verbal statement (qawl), is given precedence over the reported action (fi'l) of the Prophet praying in darkness, because in Hanafi usul, a statement overrides an action when they appear contradictory. The Shafi'i interpretation that the hadith merely means to pray when dawn is certain is rejected by the apparent wording.

Key Terms
إسفار (isfār): The time when light appears and whiteness spreads in the sky, before sunrise.
تغليس (taghlīs): Praying Fajr in darkness, close to dawn.
ترتيل (tartīl): Measured, clear recitation of the Qur'an, giving each letter its due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hadith 'Asfiru bi'l-fajr' considered to indicate recommendation (istihbab) rather than obligation (wujub) in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the hadith is weak in transmission.
B) Because the attached phrase 'fa-innahu a'zam li'l-ajr' shows the reason is reward, which diverts from obligation.
C) Because the Prophet's action of praying in darkness abrogates the command.
D) Because it is a hadith ahad and cannot indicate obligation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends isfar for men's Fajr due to the hadith's wording, but taghlis is recommended for women and for Fajr at Muzdalifah.

Ruling on Isfar for Fajr: Hanafi Proofs and Exceptions
Ruling and proofs for delaying Fajr prayer until light, with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on isfar for Fajr prayer, identify the proof (hadith and usul principle), and apply the exceptions for women and Muzdalifah.

Core Idea
Isfar (delay until light) is recommended for men's Fajr; verbal hadith outweighs the Prophet's practice in Hanafi usul.

Should a man delay the Fajr prayer until the sky is bright, or is it better to pray in the dark? The Hanafi school has a nuanced position based on a specific prophetic hadith and the principle that verbal commands take precedence over actions. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and key exceptions for women and pilgrims at Muzdalifah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The commentator states that isfar (delaying until brightness) for Fajr is al-masnoon (recommended). Note that this is a sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
The term 'masnoon' in this context indicates a recommended act.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر' (Make Fajr bright, for it is greater in reward). The commentator cites its narrators and multiple chains.
This is a hadith ahad (solitary report), but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'أسفروا' indicates a command. However, the attached clause 'فإنه أعظم للأجر' (for it is greater in reward) diverts the command from obligation to recommendation. The word 'greater' implies it is not obligatory, otherwise the reward would be equal.
This is a classic Hanafi usul application: a command followed by a motivating reason is often interpreted as recommendation.
4
Note the dispute and refutation
The Shafi'is interpret the hadith to mean 'pray at the certainty of dawn, not before', not delaying. The commentator refutes this by pointing to the apparent wording 'أسفروا' which means to make it bright, implying delay.
The Hanafi school prefers the verbal hadith over the narrated action of the Prophet (praying in darkness) based on the usul principle that qawl takes precedence over fi'l.
5
Apply the exceptions
Two exceptions: (1) For the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah, taghlis (praying in darkness) is recommended, based on authentic reports. (2) For women, taghlis is always recommended because darkness is more concealing.
These exceptions show that the ruling is contextual, not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : أسفرُوا بالفَجْرِ، فَإِنَّهُ أَعْظَمُ للآخر» عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية المسنون فيه، ثمّ إعادة صلاة الفجر مع طهارة ، ومع الترتيل المذكور لـو ظهر فساد صلاته بفساد فيها أو في طهارتها، كل ذلك قبل طلوع الشمس، فإنّه لو أسفر جداً وصلى ثم ظهر فساد صلاته بنسيان الغُسلِ من الجنابة أو الوضوء أو غير ذلك، لم تكن إعادته في الوقت. وهذا كله للرجال الغير الحجاج المصلين بمزدلفة، فإنه يستثنى منه صبح مزدلفة ؛ ، إذ لا يستحب لها الإسفار بل التغليس بذلك وردت الأخبار أنه صلاها هناك بغلس ؛ أخرجه البخاري وغيره وذكر في الدر المختار) وغيره : أن المرأة يستحب لها التغليس مطلقاً ؛ لأنّ الظلام أستر في حقها. [١] قوله : قال له هذا الحديث أخرجه البزار والطحاوي والطبراني وابن ماجة وأبو داود والترمذي والنسائي وغيرهم بطرق مختلفة بألفاظ متقاربة)، وظاهر الأمر فيه وإن كان للوجوب لكن ما يليه وهو قوله : فإنّه أعظم للأجر صرفه عن الوجوب إلى الاستحباب. ولما كان هذا الحديث قوليَّاً رُجح على ما رواه أصحاب الصحاح «أنه صلى الصبح بغلس (۳) ؛ لأن القول مقدَّم على الفعل كما تقرّر في كتب الأصول، وتأويله بأن المراد به : صلوا عند ظهور الصبح الصادق والتيقن به لا قبله، ولا في وقت تردد فيه بين ظهوره وعدم ظهوره، كما نقل عن الشافعيّة يردّه ظاهر عبارة الحديث.
He said: 'Make Fajr bright (i.e., delay it until it is light), for it is greater in reward.' (The text) 'Umda al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya: It is recommended (al-masnoon) therein, then repetition of Fajr prayer with purity and with the mentioned slow recitation if the invalidity of his prayer appears due to corruption in it or in its purity, all that before sunrise. For if he delayed much and prayed then the invalidity of his prayer appeared due to forgetting the ghusl from janaba or wudu or other than that, his repetition would not be within the time. And all this is for men who are not pilgrims and who pray at Muzdalifah, for the morning prayer of Muzdalifah is excluded from it, for isfar is not recommended for it but rather taghlis (praying in darkness); reports have come that he prayed there in darkness; al-Bukhari and others narrated it. And it is mentioned in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others: for a woman, taghlis is recommended absolutely, because darkness is more concealing for her. [1] His statement: This hadith was narrated by al-Bazzar, al-Tahawi, al-Tabarani, Ibn Majah, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i and others with various chains and close wordings. The apparent imperative form, although it indicates obligation, but what follows it, namely 'for it is greater in reward', diverts it from obligation to recommendation. And since this hadith is verbal, it is given precedence over what the scholars of the authentic collections narrated: 'that he prayed the morning prayer in darkness', because the verbal takes precedence over the actual, as established in the books of usul. And the interpretation that the intent is 'pray at the appearance of the true dawn and certainty of it, not before it, nor in a time of doubt between its appearance and non-appearance', as transmitted from the Shafi'is, is refuted by the apparent wording of the hadith.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'أسفروا بالفجر' from the matn. The commentator explains that it is recommended to delay the Fajr prayer until the light is clear, based on the hadith 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر'. The hadith is narrated by multiple chains. The imperative form is diverted from obligation to recommendation by the attached reason 'greater reward'. This verbal hadith is preferred over the actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) where he prayed Fajr in darkness, because in Hanafi usul, a verbal command takes precedence over an action in deducing rulings. The Shafi'i interpretation that the hadith means to pray at the certitude of dawn is refuted because the evident meaning of the hadith is to delay until brightness. The commentator then notes exceptions: the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah (for pilgrims) is recommended to be performed in darkness (taghlis), and for women, taghlis is always recommended for modesty. The passage also discusses a scenario where a person delays Fajr, prays, and later discovers that his prayer was invalid due to a missed ritual bath or wudu; in that case, he does not repeat the prayer within the time because the time for repetition has passed if he prayed after the delay. This ruling applies to men who are not pilgrims at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
الإسفار (al-isfar): Delaying the Fajr prayer until the light appears clearly, such that one can discern the whiteness of dawn.
التغليس (al-taghlis): Praying Fajr while it is still dark, i.e., before the brightness of dawn becomes widespread.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the hadith 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر' considered evidence for recommendation, not obligation?
A) Because the imperative form is weak in authority.
B) Because the phrase 'greater reward' diverts the command from obligation to recommendation.
C) Because the Prophet's action of praying in darkness abrogates it.
D) Because the hadith is a solitary report.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends isfar (delay until light) for men's Fajr prayer, with exceptions for women and Muzdalifah, based on a verbal hadith that outweighs the Prophet's practice in darkness.

Ruling on Delaying Dhuhr in Summer (Ibrad)
Ruling and proof for delaying Dhuhr prayer until coolness in summer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ibrad, explain its proof from hadith, and refute the Shafi'i counter-interpretation based on the passage.

Core Idea
Ibrad is recommended, not obligatory; the hadith command is for preference, proven by the Prophet's practice.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on delaying the Dhuhr prayer in summer (ibrad). The passage clarifies that ibrad is a sunnah, not a fard, and addresses an intra-Hanafi restriction and an inter-madhhab disagreement. By understanding the proof from hadith and the reasoning behind it, you will be able to apply this ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is ibrad? What is its hukm (sunnah)? The passage states it is 'mustahabb' (recommended).
The act is delaying Dhuhr until coolness in summer.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'أَبْرِدُوا بِالصَّلاةِ فَإِنَّ شِدَّةَ الْحَرِّ مِنْ فَيْحِ جَهَنَّمَ'.
This is a direct command from the Prophet.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the imperative indicate recommendation, not obligation? The context and other narrations show it is for preference, not compulsion.
The rationale (علة) is the severe heat from Hellfire.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some earlier scholars restricted ibrad to congregational prayers in hot climates. The later view (al-Bahr) says it is absolute.
The mufta bihi is absolute recommendation based on the generality of the narrations.
5
Refute the Shafi'i interpretation
Some Shafi'is claim the hadith means to pray in the heat itself. The passage shows this is invalidated by multiple narrations and the Prophet's practice.
The commentator states 'وبذا يبطل تأويل بعض الشافعية'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١] قوله : والتأخير؛ أي يستحبُّ التأخيرُ للظهر أيام الصيف ، وقيده في «الجوهرة»(۲) و«السراج الوهاج شرح مختصر القدوري بما إذا كان يصلي بجماعة في مسجد، وأن يكون في البلاد الحارّة، وأن يكون في شدَّة الحرّ، وردّه صاحب «البحر» وغيره، وأفتوا باستحباب الإبرادِ مطلقاً ؛ لإطلاق الروايات، وحده أن يصلّي قبل المثل. [٢]قوله : في «صحيح البخاري) ، وكذا رواه مسلم وابن ماجة والنسائي وابن خزيمة وغيرهم. وفي صحيح البخاري» أيضاً : «كان رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا اشتد الحر أبرد ، وإذا اشتد البرد عجل»، وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة قولية وفعليّة، وبهذا يبطل تأويل بعض الشافعية أن المراد به صلّوا في وقت الحرّ، وأبردوا الحرارة بسبب أداء الصلاة. وفي «مجمع البحار»: الفيح : شيوع الحرّ، ويقال : الفوح، مـن فـاحـت القـدر تفوح وتفيح : إذا غلت، وهو عله شرعيّة الإبراد، فإنّ شدته يسلب الخشوع، أو لأنه وقت غضب الله ، فلا ينجح فيه الطلب بالمناجاة.
[1] His statement: 'And delay for Dhuhr of summer'; meaning, delay is recommended for Dhuhr in summer days. It is restricted in al-Jawhara and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri to when he prays in congregation in a mosque, and that it be in hot lands, and that it be in severe heat. But the author of al-Bahr and others refuted this and gave fatwa on the recommendation of ibrad (delaying) absolutely, because of the generality of the narrations. Its limit is that he prays before the shadow becomes equal (i.e., before the time of the second zawaal). [2] His statement: 'In Sahih al-Bukhari' and likewise narrated by Muslim, Ibn Majah, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzaymah and others. Also in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, when the heat was severe, he would delay (ibrād); and when the cold was severe, he would hasten.' And on this topic there are many verbal and actual reports. And by this, the interpretation of some Shafi'is that the intent is 'pray in the time of heat, and cool down the heat by performing prayer' is invalidated. And in Majma' al-Bihar: 'al-Fayh' means the spreading of heat, and it is said 'al-Fawh' from 'fāḥat al-qidr tafūḥu wa tafīḥu' if it boils. And it is the reason for the legislation of ibrad, for its severity deprives one of khushu', or because it is a time of Allah's anger, and supplication is not successful during it.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn phrase 'والتأخير لظهر الصيف' (and delay for Dhuhr of summer). The commentator explains that it is recommended to delay the Dhuhr prayer in summer until the heat subsides; this is called ibrad. There is a disagreement: some scholars like the author of al-Jawhara restrict this to congregational prayers in mosques and hot climates. But the author of al-Bahr prefers the absolute recommendation based on the general nature of the hadith. The limit of delay is that the prayer must be performed before the shadow becomes equal to the object's height (i.e., before the entrance of Asr time). The primary proof is the hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'أَبْرِدُوا بِالصَّلاةِ فَإِنَّ شِدَّةَ الْحَرِّ مِنْ فَيْحِ جَهَنَّمَ' (Delay the prayer, for severe heat is from the expansion of Hell). There are also reports of the Prophet's practice. This refutes the Shafi'i interpretation that the hadith means to pray in the heat but that the prayer itself cools the heat. The commentator also gives the wisdom behind ibrad: extreme heat prevents khushu' (concentration) and it is a time when Allah is angry, so supplication may not be accepted.

Key Terms
الإبراد (al-ibrad): Delaying the Dhuhr prayer in summer until the heat subsides and it becomes cooler.
الفيح (al-fayh): The spreading of heat, as from the expansion of Hellfire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pray as early as possible.
B) Delay until the shadow becomes equal to the object (i.e., until Asr time).
C) Delay until the heat subsides, but before the shadow equals the object.
D) Pray immediately at the start of Dhuhr time.

Key Takeaway
Ibrad (delaying Dhuhr in summer) is a sunnah muakkadah, recommended absolutely, with the limit that it be before the shadow becomes equal.

Ruling on Delaying Asr Prayer
Ruling on the recommendation to delay Asr prayer until the sun begins to change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for Asr prayer and identify when delaying becomes disliked (makruh) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Delaying Asr until the sun changes is disliked; the recommended delay is moderate, not extreme.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the preferred time for Asr prayer. While it is recommended to delay Asr slightly from its earliest time, this recommendation does not extend to the point where the sun begins to change color. The passage clarifies the distinction between a recommended delay and a disliked one, supported by a well-known hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under consideration is performing the Asr prayer within its time. The ruling distinguishes between two periods: the preferred time (before the sun changes) and the disliked time (after change).
2
Locate the dalil
The narrator cites the hadith: 'That is the prayer of the hypocrites' (تلك صلاة المنافقين). This is a well-known hadith regarding praying Asr at the very end of its time.
The hadith is cited as proof that delaying until the sun changes is blameworthy.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet described delaying Asr until the sun turns yellow as the practice of hypocrites. By analogy, any delay that reaches that point is disliked. The Hanafi school uses this to set a boundary: before change is fine; after change is makruh.
The imperative to avoid hypocrisy implies dislike (karahah).
4
Note the ikhtilaf on estimation
Some Hanafi scholars (al-Nakha'i, al-Thawri, al-Hakim al-Shahid) consider the change in the sun's light itself, not just shadow length. Abu Hanifa disliked delaying until change. The core ruling—that praying after change is disliked—is agreed upon.
The difference is about the precise moment of change, not the ruling itself.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The operative position (mufta bihi) is that it is recommended to delay Asr moderately, but one should not delay until the sun turns yellow. That delay is makruh tanzihan.
The relied-upon view is derived from the consensus (ittifaq) that praying after change is disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣]قوله : وللعصر ؛ أي يستحب للعصر شتاء كان أو صيفاً، إلا في يوم غيم أن يؤخّر عن أوّل وقته ما لم تتغيّر الشمس، وقدره بعضهم بأنه إذا بقي مقدار رمح لم يتغير، ودونه يتغير، وعن النخعي والثوري : إنه يعتبر التغير في ضوئها، وبه قال الحاكم الشهيد، فإذا جاءَ التغير كره أداء الصلاة اتفاقاً. قال الإمام محمد له في كتاب الحجج»: «قال أبو حنيفة : تأخير صلاة العصر إلى تغير الشمس كان يكرهه، لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «تلك صلاة المنافقين» والحديث مشهور.
[3] His statement: 'And for Asr'; meaning, it is recommended for Asr, whether winter or summer, except on a cloudy day, that it be delayed from its beginning time as long as the sun has not changed. And some estimated it: if there remains a spear's length [i.e., the shadow] it has not changed, and less than that it changes. From al-Nakha'i and al-Thawri: indeed, the change is considered in its light; and al-Hakim al-Shahid said the same. When the change comes, it is disliked (kariha) to perform the prayer by agreement. Imam Muhammad said in his book al-Hujaj: 'Abu Hanifa said: Delaying Asr prayer until the sun's change he used to dislike it, because the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'That is the prayer of the hypocrites' and the hadith is well-known.'
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn phrase 'وللعصر ما لم تتغير الشمس' (and for Asr, as long as the sun has not changed). The commentator explains that it is recommended to delay Asr prayer from its earliest time until the sun begins to change (i.e., it takes on a yellowish hue). This is recommended in all seasons except on cloudy days, where one should pray earlier. Some scholars estimate the limit as the length of a spear's shadow: if the shadow is longer than a spear, the sun has not changed; if shorter, it has. Other scholars like al-Nakha'i and al-Thawri consider the change in the sun's light itself. Once the sun changes, it is disliked to pray Asr by consensus. The commentator then reports from Imam Muhammad that Abu Hanifa disliked delaying Asr until the sun changes, citing the hadith 'That is the prayer of the hypocrites' — meaning delaying it to the very end. This indicates that while delaying Asr is recommended to a degree, delaying it to the point of the sun's change is disliked. The correct understanding is that it is recommended to delay slightly, but not until the sun turns yellow; rather, the recommendation is to pray before that disliked time.

Key Terms
تغير الشمس (taghayyur al-shams): The change of the sun from its white/brilliant color to a yellowish hue, indicating that the preferred time is ending.
الكراهة (al-karahah): It is disliked (makruh) to perform a prayer at a certain time; here it is agreed upon when the sun changes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Delaying Asr prayer moderately is recommended, but delaying until the sun changes color is disliked (makruh) based on the hadith of the hypocrites' prayer.

Delaying Zuhr and Asr: Hanafi Preferences and the Asr Dispute
Hanafi commentary on preferred times with inter-madhhab dispute on Asr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Zuhr in summer and Asr, identify the primary proofs, and explain the inter-madhhab dispute on Asr timing.

Core Idea
Delay Zuhr in summer heat and Asr while the sun is white — but the Asr dispute has strong opposing hadith.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the recommended times for Zuhr and Asr prayers according to the Hanafi school. It begins with the well-known hadith 'Cool yourselves with prayer' for Zuhr in summer, then addresses a significant disagreement with the Maliki and Shafi'i schools regarding the best time for Asr. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh competing evidences and appreciate legitimate ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on Zuhr delay
Locate the statement that delaying Zuhr in summer is recommended (mustahabb). Note the conditions and the primary proof from Sahih al-Bukhari.
The text uses 'yustahabb' and cites the hadith 'أبردوا بالصلاة'.
2
Analyze the Asr ruling and its conditions
Find the Hanafi view that delaying Asr is preferred as long as the sun has not changed color. Note the exception for cloudy days and the estimated limit (length of a spear).
The phrase 'ما لم تتغير الشمس' is key.
3
Examine the inter-madhhab dispute on Asr
Read the passage quoting Imam Muhammad's Kitab al-Hujaj. Contrast Abu Hanifa's position (delay) with that of Malik and the people of Medina (hastening). Identify the proofs for each side.
The Hanafi proof: practice of Ibn Mas'ud's companions and benefit of nafl prayers. Maliki proof: hadiths of the Prophet hastening Asr.
4
Evaluate the resolution of the dispute
Note how the commentator (Mulla 'Ali al-Qari) acknowledges the authentic hadiths for hastening but still leans toward the Hanafi view, referring further investigation to other works.
The text says 'لولا ورود الأحاديث الصحيحة...' indicating the strength of opposing evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة/ أوقات الصلاة
والتأخير لظهر الصيف، وللعصر ما لم تتغير الشمس

( ) والتأخير الظهر الصيف) ، في «صحيح البُخَارِي»: «أَبْرِدُوا بِالصَّلاة، فَإِنَّ شِدَّةَ الحَرِّ مِنْ فَيْحِ جَهَنَّم» ، (وللعصر" ما لم تتغير الشمس
[١] قوله : والتأخير؛ أي يستحبُّ التأخيرُ للظهر أيام الصيف ، وقيده في «الجوهرة»(۲) و«السراج الوهاج شرح مختصر القدوري بما إذا كان يصلي بجماعة في وأن يكون في البلاد الحارّة، وأن يكون في شدَّة الحرّ، وردّه صاحب «البحر» مسجد، وغيره، وأفتوا باستحباب الإبرادِ مطلقاً ؛ لإطلاق الروايات، وحده أن يصلّي قبل المثل. [٢]قوله : في «صحيح البخاري) ، وكذا رواه مسلم وابن ماجة والنسائي وابن خزيمة وغيرهم.
وفي صحيح البخاري» أيضاً : «كان رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا اشتد الحر أبرد ، وإذا اشتد البرد عجل»، وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة قولية وفعليّة، وبهذا يبطل تأويل بعض الشافعية أن المراد به صلّوا في وقت الحرّ، وأبردوا الحرارة بسبب أداء الصلاة.
وفي «مجمع البحار»: الفيح : شيوع الحرّ، ويقال : الفوح، مـن فـاحـت القـدر تفوح وتفيح : إذا غلت، وهو عله شرعيّة الإبراد، فإنّ شدته يسلب الخشوع، أو لأنه وقت غضب الله ، فلا ينجح فيه الطلب بالمناجاة.
[٣]قوله : وللعصر ؛ أي يستحب للعصر شتاء كان أو صيفاً، إلا في يوم غيم أن يؤخّر عن أوّل وقته ما لم تتغيّر الشمس، وقدره بعضهم بأنه إذا بقي مقدار رمح لم يتغير، ودونه يتغير، وعن النخعي والثوري : إنه يعتبر التغير في ضوئها، وبه قال الحاكم الشهيد، فإذا جاءَ التغير كرة أداء الصلاة اتفاقاً.
قال الإمام محمد له في كتاب الحجج»: «قال أبو حنيفة : تأخير صلاة العصر أفضلُ من تعجيلها إذا صُلِّيت والشمس بيضاء نقية لم تتغير، وعلى هذا كان أصحاب عبد الله بن مسعود له بالكوفة ، أخبرنا محمد بن أبان بن صالح . حماد . عن. عن إبراهيم النخعي له قال : أدركتُ أصحاب ابن مسعود الله يصلون العصر في آخر وقتها. وقال أهل المدينة ومالك الله : التعجيلُ بها أفضلُ من تأخيرها ، قال محمد : قد جاءت في هذا آثار ، فأما ما عليه أصحاب ابن مسعود له فالتأخير». انتهى وعلل صاحب «الهداية وغيره أفضلية التأخير بأنّ فيه تكثير النوافل ؛ لكراهتها بعد صلاة العصر، وهـو تعليل حسن حقيق بأن يؤخذ به، وكذا الاتباع بأصحاب عبد الله حسن لولا ورودِ الأحاديث الصحيحة المرويَّة في السنن والصحيحين وغيرها الدالة على أنّ النبي الله وعامة أصحابه الله كانوا يعجلون العصر، وقد ذكرنا نبذاً من تحقيق هذه المسألة في «التعليق الممجد» وزيادته مفوضة إلى «السعاية».
Book of Prayer / Times of Prayer. And delaying Zuhr in summer, and for Asr as long as the sun has not changed. ( ) And delaying Zuhr in summer, in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'Cool yourselves with prayer, for the intensity of heat is from the blazing of Hell.' And for Asr as long as the sun has not changed. [1] He said: 'And delaying' means it is recommended to delay Zuhr in summer days. It was restricted in al-Jawhara and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri to when one prays in congregation and in hot countries and in extreme heat, but the author of al-Bahr rejected that and they gave fatwa of the recommendation of cooling absolutely, due to the generality of narrations. Its limit is to pray before the shadow becomes like the object. [2] He said: In Sahih al-Bukhari, and also narrated by Muslim, Ibn Majah, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzaymah and others. Also in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'When the heat was intense, the Messenger of Allah would delay (cool) the prayer, and when it was cold, he would hasten it.' There are many verbal and practical traditions on this, and this refutes the interpretation of some Shafi'is that it means pray in the heat and cool the heat by performing the prayer. In Majma' al-Bihar: al-Fayh means the spreading of heat, also said al-Fawh, from the pot boiling, and it is the cause for the legislation of cooling, because its intensity takes away humility, or because it is a time of Allah's wrath, so supplication does not succeed. [3] He said: 'And for Asr' meaning it is recommended for Asr, winter or summer, except on a cloudy day, to delay from its beginning time as long as the sun has not changed. Some estimated it as when the measure of a spear remains it has not changed, and less than that it changes. From al-Nakha'i and al-Thawri: change is considered in its light, and al-Hakim al-Shahid said so. When change occurs, it is disliked to perform the prayer by agreement. Imam Muhammad said in Kitab al-Hujaj: 'Abu Hanifa said: Delaying Asr prayer is better than hastening it when it is prayed while the sun is white and pure, not changed. On this were the companions of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud in Kufa. Muhammad ibn Aban ibn Salih informed us, Hammad, from, from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i who said: I met the companions of Ibn Mas'ud praying Asr at its last time. The people of Medina and Malik said: Hastening it is better than delaying it. Muhammad said: Traditions have come on this, but what the companions of Ibn Mas'ud are upon is delay.' End. The author of al-Hidayah and others explained the superiority of delay as multiplying supererogatory prayers, because they are disliked after Asr prayer. This is a good explanation, worthy of being adopted. Likewise following the companions of Abdullah is good, were it not for the authentic hadiths narrated in the Sunan and Sahihain and other books indicating that the Prophet and most of his companions used to hasten Asr. We have mentioned a sample of the investigation of this issue in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad, and its full discussion is delegated to al-Si'ayah.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the preferred times for Zuhr and Asr prayers from the Hanafi perspective, with a detailed inter-madhhab dispute on Asr. The author first explains that delaying Zuhr in summer is recommended (mustahabb) based on the hadith 'Cool yourselves with prayer' and other narrations. He notes that some scholars restricted this recommendation to congregational prayer in hot climates, but the stronger view is absolute recommendation. The limit is to pray before the shadow becomes equal to the object (i.e., before the time of the shadow's lengthening passes). The author then addresses a misinterpretation by some Shafi'is that the hadith means to pray in the heat itself, and refutes it. For Asr, the Hanafi position is that it is recommended to delay Asr as long as the sun has not changed color (i.e., not turned yellow). This applies winter and summer except on cloudy days. The limit is when the shadow reaches the length of a spear; before that it is unchanged, after that it changes. The author cites the opinion of Abu Hanifa through Imam Muhammad that delaying Asr is better when the sun is still white and pure, and that this was the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud's companions. The people of Medina (including Imam Malik) preferred hastening Asr. Imam Muhammad notes that there are traditions on both sides, but follows the Kufan practice. The commentator then adds that al-Hidayah's reasoning for preferring delay is to increase supererogatory prayers since they are disliked after Asr, but acknowledges that authentic hadiths show the Prophet and his companions generally hastened Asr. This leaves the issue somewhat open, with the full discussion referred to other works. The Hanafi position remains that delay is recommended (not obligatory) and the mufta bihi is the permissibility of both, with delay being better under certain conditions.

Key Terms
إبراد (ibrad): To delay the prayer until the cooler part of the day, specifically for Zuhr in summer.
فيح (fayh): The spreading or intensity of heat, from the root f-y-h meaning to boil or spread.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on delaying Zuhr prayer in summer?
A) It is obligatory to delay.
B) It is recommended (mustahabb) to delay.
C) It is prohibited to delay.
D) It is makruh to delay.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying Zuhr in summer and Asr while the sun is white, but the Asr ruling is disputed with strong opposing evidence from authentic hadiths.

Recommended Times for Isha and Witr
Commentary on recommended times for Isha (to third of night) and Witr (to end of night)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended times for Isha and Witr prayers, identify their proof from hadith, and explain the wisdom and conditions for delaying Witr.

Core Idea
Delay Isha to the first third of the night and Witr to the end, but only if you are sure to wake for Witr.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the preferred times for two prayers: Isha and Witr. The commentator clarifies that delaying these prayers is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, based on explicit hadith evidence. The wisdom includes fostering congregation and discouraging idle talk after Isha. For Witr, a crucial condition is added: one must be confident of waking up; otherwise, early performance is better.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage discusses the timing for Isha and Witr prayers. Determine that the ruling is 'mustahabb' (recommended) based on the commentary's explicit use of 'yustahabb'.
Not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil for Isha
Find the hadith: 'Were it not that I would burden my community, I would order them to delay Isha to the third of the night.' Recognize that this proves the recommendation.
Also the narration mentioning 'half of it'.
3
Locate the dalil for Witr
Find the hadiths: 'Make the last of your prayers at night Witr' and the narration about fear of not waking. These show the flexibility.
The phrase 'prayer at the end of the night is witnessed' highlights virtue.
4
Extract the wisdom (hikma)
For Isha: to increase congregation and cut off idle talk (samar). For Witr: to ensure it is the last prayer and to be witnessed.
Idle talk after Isha is makruh.
5
Note the condition for Witr delay
Delay is only recommended if one is safe from missing Witr and trusts his waking. If not, early performance is better.
The condition is explicit in the hadith.

قوله : وللعشاء؛ أي يستحب تأخيرُ صلاة العشاء صيفاً كان أو شتاءً إلى ثلث الليل الأوّل ؛ لحديث: «لولا أن أشق على أمتي لأمرتهم بتأخير العشاء إلى ثلث الليل»، وفي رواية: «ونصفه» (١) ، أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة وأبو داود والبزار وغيرهم، والسر فيه تكثير الجماعة، وقطع السمر وهو الحديث الدنيوي الممنوع عنه بعد صلاة العشاء، لما روى الستَّةُ : « أنَّ النبي الهلال لو كان يكره النوم قبلها، والحديث بعدها»(۳). (٢) قوله : وللوتر؛ أي يستحب تأخيره إلى آخر الليل إن أمن من فوته واعتمد انتباهه وإلا فأداؤه أوله الحديث : اجعلوا آخر صلاتكم بالليل وتراً)، أخرجه الشيخان، ولحديث: «من خاف منكم أن لا يستيقظ من آخر الليل فليوتـر مـن أوّل الليل، ومن طمع منكم أن يستيقظ فليوتر آخر الليل ، فإنّ صلاة آخر الليل مشهودة،
He said: 'And for Isha' meaning it is recommended to delay Isha prayer, whether summer or winter, to the first third of the night, due to the hadith: 'Were it not that I would burden my community, I would order them to delay Isha to the third of the night.' And in a narration: 'and half of it' - narrated by Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Abu Dawud, al-Bazzar, and others. The wisdom in it is to increase the congregation and to cut off night talk (samar), which is worldly conversation prohibited after Isha prayer, as narrated by the Six: 'The Prophet disliked sleep before it and conversation after it.' (2) He said: 'And for Witr' meaning it is recommended to delay it to the end of the night if one is safe from missing it and trusts his waking; otherwise, performing it at its beginning is better, due to the hadith: 'Make the last of your prayers at night Witr' - narrated by the two Shaykhs, and the hadith: 'Whoever among you fears that he will not wake up at the end of the night, let him pray Witr at the beginning of the night, and whoever among you hopes to wake up, let him pray Witr at the end of the night, for the prayer at the end of the night is witnessed.'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage addresses the preferred times for Isha and Witr prayers. The commentator explains that it is recommended (mustahabb) to delay Isha until the first third of the night, regardless of season. This is based on a hadith where the Prophet expressed a desire to make delay obligatory but refrained out of mercy. The wisdom includes increasing the congregation size and discouraging idle talk after Isha. The prohibition of sleep before Isha and conversation after it is also mentioned to emphasize the virtue of performing it in its preferred time. For Witr, the recommendation is to delay it until the very end of the night, provided one is certain of waking up. If there is fear of missing it, one should pray it earlier. The evidence comes from the Prophet's command to make Witr the last prayer and the hadith distinguishing between those who can reliably wake up and those who cannot. The phrase 'prayer at the end of the night is witnessed' indicates the superiority of late-night prayer. The Hanafi position is clear: delay is better for those who can, otherwise early performance is acceptable.

Key Terms
السمر (al-samar): Nighttime conversation, especially worldly talk, which is discouraged after Isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) In all cases.

C) Only on summer nights.
D) Only if one prays in congregation.

Key Takeaway
Delaying Isha and Witr is recommended, not obligatory, with Witr delay conditioned on assurance of waking.

Preferred Times for 'Isha, Witr, and 'Asr (Hanafi View with Dispute)
Commentary on delaying 'Isha and Witr, and the 'Asr timing dispute between Hanafis and Madinese

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on delaying 'Isha and Witr, and evaluate the dispute between Hanafis and Madinese regarding 'Asr timing by comparing the proofs on both sides.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school delays 'Asr to multiply nawafil, but the Madinese hasten it following the Prophet's practice — both have valid proofs.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'ayah' explains the recommended timings for 'Isha and Witr prayers, and then delves into a disputed issue: whether it is better to hasten or delay the 'Asr prayer when the sun is still white. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud's companions in Kufa and the reasoning that delaying allows more supererogatory prayers, holds that delay is better. In contrast, the people of Medina, led by Imam Malik, argue that hastening 'Asr is superior, citing authentic hadiths that the Prophet and his Companions hastened it. The author presents both sides and acknowledges the tension, leaving the issue with a nuanced stance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for 'Isha and Witr
Determine the recommended times from the hadith evidence: 'Isha until one-third of the night, Witr delayed until end of night if confident of waking.
2
Extract the 'Asr timing dispute
Note that Hanafis say delaying 'Asr is better (afdal) when the sun is white; Madinese say hastening is better.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The proof from the practice of Ibn Mas'ud's companions and the reasoning (ta'lil) from al-Hidayah: increasing nawafil because they are disliked after 'Asr.
4
Analyze the Madinese proof
The authentic hadiths in Sahihain and Sunan showing the Prophet and his Companions hastened 'Asr.
5
Evaluate the author's stance
The author notes the strength of both proofs and refers to his other works; no decisive tarjih is given, indicating the issue's complexity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية
وللعشاء إلى ثلث الليل ، وللوتر إلى آخر وقته لِمَنْ وَثق بالانتباه فحسب وللعشاء" إلى ثلث الليل ، وللوتر " إلى آخر وقتِه لِمَنْ وَثَقَ بالانتباه فحسب العصر أفضلُ من تعجيلها إذا صُلِّيت والشمس بيضاء نقية لم تتغير، وعلى هذا كان أصحاب عبد الله بن مسعود له بالكوفة ، أخبرنا محمد بن أبان بن صالح . حماد. عن. عن إبراهيم النخعي له قال : أدركتُ أصحاب ابن مسعود الله يصلون العصر في آخر وقتها. وقال أهل المدينة ومالك الله : التعجيلُ بها أفضلُ من تأخيرها ، قال محمد : قد جاءت في هذا آثار ، فأما ما عليه أصحاب ابن مسعود له فالتأخير». انتهى وعلل صاحب «الهداية وغيره أفضلية التأخير بأنّ فيه تكثير النوافل ؛ لكراهتها بعد صلاة العصر، وهـو تعليل حسن حقيق بأن يؤخذ به، وكذا الاتباع بأصحاب عبد الله حسن لولا ورودِ الأحاديث الصحيحة المرويَّة في السنن والصحيحين وغيرها الدالة على أنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعامة أصحابه الله كانوا يعجلون العصر، وقد ذكرنا نبذاً من تحقيق هذه المسألة في «التعليق الممجد» وزيادته مفوضة إلى «السعاية».
[١]قوله : وللعشاء ؛ أي يستحب تأخيرُ صلاة العشاء صيفاً كان أو شتاءً إلى ثلث الليل الأوّل ؛ لحديث: «لولا أن أشق على أمتي لأمرتهم بتأخير العشاء إلى ثلث الليل»، وفي رواية: «ونصفه» (١) ، أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة وأبو داود والبزار وغيرهم، والسر فيه تكثير الجماعة، وقطع السمر وهو الحديث الدنيوي الممنوع عنه بعد صلاة العشاء، لما روى الستَّةُ : « أنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يكره النوم قبلها، والحديث بعدها»(۳). (٢) قوله : وللوتر؛ أي يستحب تأخيره إلى آخر الليل إن أمن من فوته واعتمد انتباهه وإلا فأداؤه أوله الحديث : اجعلوا آخر صلاتكم بالليل وتراً)، أخرجه الشيخان، ولحديث: «من خاف منكم أن لا يستيقظ من آخر الليل فليوتـر مـن أوّل الليل، ومن طمع منكم أن يستيقظ فليوتر آخر الليل ، فإنّ صلاة آخر الليل مشهودة، وذلك أفضل ) ، أخرجه مسلم وأحمد.
Foundation of the Care on the Explanation of the Protection. And for 'Isha (prayer, it is recommended to delay) up to one-third of the night, and for Witr up to the end of its time for one who trusts his awakening only. 'Asr is better than performing it early when prayed while the sun is white, pure, unchanged. And upon this were the companions of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) in Kufa. Muhammad ibn Aban ibn Salih informed us: Hammad narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: I found the companions of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) praying 'Asr at its last time. And the people of Medina and Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) said: Performing it early is better than delaying it. Muhammad said: Reports have come on this. As for what the companions of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) were upon, it is delay. End. And the author of al-Hidayah and others explained the preference for delay because it increases supererogatory prayers, since they are disliked after 'Asr prayer. This is a good reasoning, worthy of being adopted. Likewise, following the companions of Abdullah is good were it not for the authentic hadiths narrated in the Sunan, Sahihain, and others indicating that the Prophet (peace be upon him) and most of his companions (may Allah be pleased with them) used to hasten 'Asr. We have mentioned a portion of the investigation of this issue in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad, and its addition is delegated to al-Si'ayah. [1] His statement: 'And for 'Isha' means: it is recommended to delay 'Isha prayer, whether summer or winter, until the first third of the night, due to the hadith: 'Were it not that I would burden my community, I would have ordered them to delay 'Isha until the third of the night.' In another narration: 'and its half.' It was recorded by al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Abu Dawud, al-Bazzar, and others. The wisdom behind it is multiplying the congregation and cutting off socializing, which is worldly talk forbidden after 'Isha prayer, because the six (narrators) narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) disliked sleeping before it and talking after it. (2) His statement: 'And for Witr' means: it is recommended to delay it until the end of the night if one is safe from missing it and relies on his awakening, otherwise performing it at its beginning. The hadith: 'Make the last of your prayers at night Witr' recorded by the two Shaykhs, and the hadith: 'Whoever among you fears that he will not wake up at the end of the night, let him perform Witr at the beginning of the night, and whoever among you hopes to wake up, let him perform Witr at the end of the night, for the prayer at the end of the night is witnessed, and that is better' recorded by Muslim and Ahmad.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings for the preferred times of 'Isha, Witr, and 'Asr prayers. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: it is mustahab (recommended) to delay 'Isha until the first third of the night, and to delay Witr until the end of the night for one who trusts he will wake up; otherwise, early Witr is better. For 'Asr, the Hanafi view (following the companions of Ibn Mas'ud) is that it is better to delay until the sun remains white and pure, not yet yellowing. The reasoning, as explained by al-Hidayah, is that delaying 'Asr allows one to increase supererogatory prayers (nawafil) because they are disliked after 'Asr. However, the author notes that authentic hadiths show the Prophet and his companions hastening 'Asr, which creates a tension. The author refers to his other works for a detailed resolution. The commentary then details the hadith evidence for delaying 'Isha and Witr, including the famous hadith about not burdening the ummah to delay 'Isha, and the hadiths about Witr being the last prayer. The overall ruling is that these are recommended, not obligatory, delays.

Key Terms
العشاء (al-'isha'): The night prayer, consisting of 4 rakat fard. Its preferred time is to delay until one-third of the night.
الوتر (al-witr): An odd-numbered prayer (usually 3 rakat) performed after 'Isha. Its preferred time is the end of the night for one confident of waking.
النوافل (al-nawafil): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayers beyond the obligatory ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi view on delaying 'Asr is based on the practice of Ibn Mas'ud's companions and the wisdom of increasing nawafil, but the issue is nuanced due to authentic hadiths favoring haste.

Expediting Zuhr in Winter, Maghrib, and Cloudy Day Prayers
Rulings on expediting certain prayers with hadith proofs and reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommendations for expediting specific obligatory prayers and explain the hadith evidence and reasoning for each case.

Core Idea
Expediting Maghrib, Zuhr in winter, and 'Asr and 'Isha on cloudy days is mustahab; other prayers are delayed to avoid disliked times.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes which prayers should be performed at the earliest possible time and which should be delayed. While many assume that praying early is always better, this lesson reveals a nuanced approach based on prophetic hadith and practical considerations. We will examine the rulings for Zuhr in winter, Maghrib, and prayers on cloudy days, as well as the supporting evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expedited prayers
Read the text to list which prayers are recommended to be performed early: Zuhr in winter, Maghrib always, and on a cloudy day: 'Asr and 'Isha.
2
Understand the exceptions
Note that Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is not included in the recommendation for i'barad (delay due to heat); it is expedited summer and winter. Also, other prayers like Zuhr in summer and 'Isha on clear nights are delayed.
The text explicitly excludes Friday from i'barad.
3
Analyze the hadith for Maghrib
The primary proof for expediting Maghrib is the hadith: 'My community will remain in good as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine.' This indicates that early performance is a sign of communal well-being.
This hadith is recorded by Abu Dawud, al-Hakim, and Ibn Majah, with sahih rating.
4
Examine the reasoning for cloudy days
On cloudy days, 'Asr and 'Isha are expedited because delaying could cause uncertainty about the time or lead to performing the prayer during a disliked period (for 'Asr) or difficulty due to rain (for 'Isha). The text states: 'in delaying 'Asr there is fear of it falling into the disliked time, therefore expediting them is recommended.'
This is based on practical reasoning (istihsan) to avoid potential harm.
5
Distinguish from summer Zuhr
In summer, Zuhr is delayed (i'barad) due to extreme heat, based on a specific hadith. This delay is not applied in winter because the heat is not a factor. The text says: 'The recommendation to delay (i.e., for Zuhr in summer due to heat) is for another reason, and does not exist in winter.'
This shows the ruling is context-dependent.

And expediting (is recommended) for Zuhr in winter, and for Maghrib, and on a cloudy day, expedite 'Asr and 'Isha, and delay other prayers. And that is better, recorded by Muslim and Ahmad. As for Friday, i'tibar (waiting for coolness) is not recommended, rather expediting both summer and winter, as stated in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. [1] His statement: 'And expediting for Zuhr in winter' because of the actual hadith mentioned, and the hadith: 'The best of deeds is prayer at its earliest time' recorded by al-Hakim and al-Tirmidhi, and the hadith: 'The first time is the pleasure of Allah' recorded by al-Bayhaqi, al-Darqutni, and al-Tirmidhi, though its chain is weak. The recommendation to delay (i.e., for Zuhr in summer due to heat) is for another reason, and does not exist in winter. [2] His statement: 'And for Maghrib' means: it is recommended to expedite it absolutely, due to the hadith: 'My community will remain in good as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine' recorded by Abu Dawud, al-Hakim (who declared it sahih), and Ibn Majah. [3] His statement: 'And delay other than them' because in delaying 'Isha there is a reduction of the congregation due to rain, and in delaying 'Asr there is a fear of it falling into the disliked time, therefore expediting them is recommended. Not so for the remaining prayers, so they are delayed to avoid occurring before their time.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings for expediting certain prayers. The matn states: expediting Zuhr in winter, Maghrib, and on a cloudy day expedite 'Asr and 'Isha, and delay other prayers. The commentary explains: For Zuhr in winter, the recommendation to expedite is due to the hadith that the best of deeds is prayer at its earliest time, and the specific hadith about Zuhr in winter (probably from the Prophet's practice). For Maghrib, it is always mustahab to expedite, as per the hadith warning against delaying until the stars appear. For 'Asr and 'Isha on cloudy days, they are expedited because if delayed, they might fall into disliked times or cause difficulty due to rain. The remaining prayers are delayed (like 'Isha on clear nights, Zuhr in summer) to avoid being too early. The commentary also notes that Friday prayer is not delayed for cooling (i'tibar) but expedited, as stated in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir.

Key Terms
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Performing the prayer at the beginning of its time, as opposed to delaying (ta'khir).
الإبراد (al-i'barad): Waiting for the coolness (of the evening) to pray Zuhr later in extreme heat. This is recommended in summer but not in winter.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends expediting Maghrib, Zuhr in winter, and prayers on cloudy days based on hadith and practical reasoning, while delaying other prayers to avoid disliked times.

Hastening and Delaying Prayers: Seasonal and Weather Considerations
Ruling on hastening/delaying prayers with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which prayers are hastened and which are delayed according to the Hanafi school, and cite the primary evidence for each ruling.

Core Idea
Hasten Zuhr in winter and Maghrib always; on cloudy days hasten Asr and Isha to avoid missing time.

This passage from *Umdat al-Ri'aya* explains the Hanafi position on when to hasten or delay the five daily prayers based on season and weather. The rulings are derived from prophetic hadiths and practical reasoning (ta'lil). Understanding these nuances helps a Muslim optimize the timing of salah in varying conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayers with specific timing rules
From the passage, list the prayers for which hastening is recommended: Zuhr in winter, Maghrib always, and on cloudy days Asr and Isha. Note that other prayers are delayed by default.
The text also mentions delaying other prayers (ghayruhuma) – these are Fajr, Zuhr in summer, and on normal days Isha and Asr.
2
Extract the evidence for each ruling
For Zuhr in winter: two hadiths (one weak) praising first-time prayer. For Maghrib: a hadith warning against delaying until stars appear. For Asr and Isha on cloudy days: reasoning – delaying Asr risks falling into makruh time, and delaying Isha may reduce congregation due to rain.
The weak hadith is still used because it is supported by other evidence.
3
Understand the exception for Zuhr in summer
The text states that delaying Zuhr (ibrad) in summer is recommended for a different reason (intense heat), which does not apply in winter. Hence, winter Zuhr is hastened, summer Zuhr is delayed.
This differentiation is a distinctive Hanafi position.
4
Analyze the strength of the evidence
All hadiths are ahad (zanni al-thubut). Hanafi usul treats such hadiths as evidence for recommendation (istihbab) not obligation, except the Maghrib hadith which has an imperative tone, but still interpreted as recommendation due to other factors.
The mufta bihi is that hastening these prayers is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.

Source Text

[١] قوله : والتعجيل لظهر الشتاء ؛ لما مر من الحديث الفعلي، ولحديث: «أفضلُ الأعمال الصلاة لأول وقتها»، أخرجه الحاكم والترمذي، ولحديث: «أول الوقتِ رضوان الله»، أخرجه البيهقي والدارقطني والترمذي ، وسنده ضعيف، وإنما استحب الإبراد في الصيف لوجه آخر، ولم يوجد في الشتاء.

And hastening for Zuhr in winter, and Maghrib, and on a cloudy day he hastens Asr and Isha, and delays others. [1] His saying: 'And hastening for Zuhr in winter' due to the practical hadith mentioned, and due to the hadith: 'The best of deeds is prayer at its first time' narrated by al-Hakim and al-Tirmidhi, and due to the hadith: 'The first time is the pleasure of Allah' narrated by al-Bayhaqi, al-Daraqutni, and al-Tirmidhi, and its chain is weak. Rather, delaying in summer is recommended for another reason, and it is not found in winter. [2] His saying: 'And Maghrib' meaning it is recommended to hasten it absolutely, due to the hadith: 'My community will remain in good as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars are intertwined' narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Hakim authenticated it, and Ibn Majah. [3] His saying: 'And he delays others' because delaying Isha reduces the congregation considering rain, and delaying Asr risks it occurring in the disliked time, therefore it is recommended to hasten them, and not so for the remaining prayers, so he delays out of caution against it occurring before the time.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the recommendation to hasten or delay certain prayers. The author explains that for Zuhr in winter, hastening is recommended based on two hadiths: one stating that the best deed is prayer at its first time, and another that the first time of prayer brings Allah's pleasure, though the latter is weak. In summer, delaying Zuhr until cooler is recommended for a different reason (intense heat), but this does not apply in winter. For Maghrib, it is always recommended to hasten it based on a hadith warning against delaying until stars appear. For Asr and Isha on cloudy days, hastening is recommended to avoid missing the time or falling into a disliked time for Asr, or to ensure congregation for Isha before rain. Other prayers (Fajr, Zuhr in summer) are delayed by default to avoid risk of being performed before their proper time. This is a standard Hanafi position derived from primary texts.

Key Terms
الإبراد (al-ibrad): Delaying Zuhr until it becomes cooler in summer.
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Hastening a prayer to its earliest time.
الوقت المكروه (al-waqt al-makruh): The disliked time for prayer, such as when the sun begins to decline until it passes the zenith, or when it becomes pale until sunset (for Asr).

Times When Prayer is Prohibited
Ruling on prohibited times for prayer with hadith proof and detailed exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited times for prayer and apply the Hanafi ruling distinguishing between voluntary and obligatory prayers.

Core Idea
Prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset is prohibited – voluntary valid but sinful, obligatory invalid unless due earlier.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya explains the three times when the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade prayer, based on the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir. It clarifies that the prohibition is one of karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitive dislike) and details which prayers are valid or invalid. Understanding this ruling is essential for every Muslim to know when to avoid prayer and when an exception applies, such as the Asr prayer of the same day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times
From the hadith: sunrise (until the sun rises high), zenith (qa'im al-dhahira, until the sun declines), and sunset (until it sets).
2
Determine the ruling
The explicit prohibition indicates karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitive dislike), not absolute impermissibility.
Hanafi usul: al-nahy yafidu al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah.
3
Distinguish voluntary from obligatory prayers
Voluntary prayers begun in these times are valid but carry karahah tahrimiyyah. Obligatory prayers (including make-up) are invalid if started during these times.
Exception: if an obligatory prayer became due earlier (e.g., Asr of the same day), it is valid at sunset.
4
Apply the exception for Asr
The Asr prayer of the current day is permissible at sunset because it became obligatory during its own time (i.e., before the prohibition set in).
Other prayers, like Fajr or Maghrib, are not exempt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة ولا يجوز صلاة ، وسجدة تلاوة ، وصلاة جنازة عند طلوعها، وقيامها، وغروبها إلا عصر يومه
[١] قوله : ولا يجوز ؛ أما عدم جواز الصلاة نفلاً كان أو فرضاً، وصلاة الجنازة ؛ فلحديث عقبة له : «ثلاث ساعات كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ينهانا أن نصلي فيه أو نقبر فيهن موتانا : حين تطلع الشمس بازغة حتى ترتفع، وحين يقوم قائم الظهيرة حتى تميل ، وحين تضيف للغروب حتى تغرب) أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة ومسلم. والمراد من النهي بقوله : (وأن نقبر صلاة الجنازة، فإنّ الدفن في هذه الأوقاتِ غير مكروه، أشار إليه الترمذي حيث أورد هذا الحديث في باب كراهية صلاة الجنازة عنه طلوع الشمس وغروبها.
وأما عدم جواز سجدة التلاوة ؛ فلأنّها في حكم الصلاة، ومعنى عدم الجواز فيها الكراهة التحريمية.
وأمّا الانعقاد وعدمُهُ ففيه تفصيل، فذكر في «الدر المختار) وغيره : أنه ينعقد نفــل بـشروع في هذه الأوقات بكراهة التحريم ، ولا ينعقد الفرضُ وما هو ملحق به، كواجب لعينه ؛ كوتر، ولا سجدة تلاوة وصلاة جنازة تليت آيتها في وقت كامل ، وحضرت الجنازة قبل هذه الأوقات ؛ لوجوبه كاملاً ، فلو وجبتا فيها لم يكره فعلهما تحريماً، ولا يخلو عن الكراهة التنزيهية.
[٢] قوله : إلا عصر يومه ؛ أي يجوز أداء عصر ذلك اليوم وقت الغروب لا غيره ، عصر اليوم الآخر ؛ لأنه وجب كاملاً ، فلا يتأدّى ناقصاً.
Section on the times in which prayer is disliked. Prayer, prostration of recitation, and funeral prayer are not permissible at its rising, its zenith, and its setting except Asr of that day. [1] His saying: 'It is not permissible' – as for the impermissibility of prayer, whether voluntary or obligatory, and funeral prayer, it is due to the hadith of Uqba: 'Three hours during which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us to pray or to bury our dead: when the sun is rising until it rises high, when the sun is at its zenith until it declines, and when it is about to set until it sets.' Narrated by the four Sunan and Muslim. And the meaning of the prohibition in his saying 'and to bury' is funeral prayer, for burial during these times is not disliked, as al-Tirmidhi pointed out when he recorded this hadith under the chapter of dislike of funeral prayer at sunrise and sunset. As for the impermissibility of prostration of recitation, it is because it is in the ruling of prayer, and the meaning of impermissibility here is tahrimi (prohibitive) dislike. As for its validity or invalidity, there is detail: it is mentioned in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others that a voluntary prayer begun in these times is valid with tahrimi dislike, but obligatory prayer and what is annexed to it, such as an obligatory-in-itself (like witr), is not valid, nor is prostration of recitation and funeral prayer if its verse was recited in complete time and the funeral was present before these times, because it is obligatory completely; if they become obligatory during these times, performing them is not tahrimi disliked, but it is not free of tanzihi dislike. [2] His saying: 'except Asr of that day' meaning it is permissible to perform Asr of that day at sunset, not other than that, nor Asr of the next day, because it became obligatory completely, so it is not performed deficiently.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the three times when prayer is prohibited: sunrise, zenith (midday when sun is at its highest point), and sunset. The primary proof is the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir forbidding prayer and burial of dead at these times. The prohibition includes all prayers – voluntary and obligatory – as well as funeral prayer and the prostration of recitation. However, the prohibition is one of karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitive dislike), not absolute prohibition in the sense of invalidity. The commentator explains that if one begins a voluntary prayer during these times, it is valid but disliked (karahah tahrimiyyah). Obligatory prayers and wajib prayers like witr are not valid if started in these times unless they are make-up prayers that became obligatory earlier. Similarly, prostration of recitation and funeral prayer are not valid if they became obligatory during a complete time (i.e., before these times) but are performed during them; if they become obligatory during these times (e.g., one recites a verse of prostration, or a funeral is present), they are not disliked in a prohibitive sense but only disliked in a lesser (tanzihi) sense. The exception is the Asr prayer of that day: it is permissible to perform it at sunset (i.e., the last part of its time) because it became obligatory while its time was valid. This is a standard Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
قائم الظهيرة (qa'im al-dhahira): The time when the sun is at its highest point at noon, when shadows disappear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing the Asr prayer of that day at sunset?
A) It is prohibited (haram).
B) It is permissible because it became obligatory completely.
C) It is invalid.
D) It is disliked but valid.

Key Takeaway
The three prohibited times are sunrise, zenith, and sunset; voluntary prayers are valid but disliked, obligatory prayers are invalid, except Asr of the same day at sunset.
