Adhan Before Time: Invalidity and the Fajr Dispute
Rules about invalid adhan before time and permissibility of Fajr adhan before dawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that adhan given before its time is invalid and must be repeated, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Fajr adhan before dawn, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Adhan is for announcing prayer time; before time it is invalid and must be repeated.

The adhan serves to inform the community that the time for a prescribed prayer has entered. When the adhan is called before the actual time, it loses its purpose and is legally ineffective. This lesson examines the ruling that such an adhan must be repeated and explores a notable dispute within the Hanafi school about whether the Fajr adhan may be called during the last half of the night, a view supported by Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i based on the hadith of Bilal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
From the passage, extract the rule that adhan given before its time is invalid and must be repeated. Note that the word 'yu'ad' indicates wajib (obligatory) repetition.
This applies to both adhan and iqama.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify the difference between Abu Hanifa (and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf regarding the permissibility of calling Fajr adhan in the last half of the night. Understand the basis of each view.
Abu Yusuf's view aligns with al-Shafi'i.
3
Examine the opposing proof (dalil)
Analyze the hadith cited by Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i: 'Bilal calls the adhan at night, so eat and drink until Ibn Umm Maktum calls the adhan.' Understand why this seems to permit an early adhan.
This hadith is in Sahih Bukhari and other collections.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the response from the majority perspective: Bilal's call was a dhikr in the form of adhan, not a proper adhan for Fajr. Another adhan (of Ibn Umm Maktum) was still required after dawn.
This response is attributed to Ibn al-Arabi in al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Identify the practical difference: if Fajr adhan is called before dawn, according to Abu Hanifa it is invalid and must be repeated; according to Abu Yusuf it is valid and no repetition is needed.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة/الأذان ۳۳ فيعادُ لو أذَّنَ قبله ، ويؤذِّنُ عالماً بالأوقات لينال الثواب فَلْيُصَلِّهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا ، فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ وَقْتها»، وعند أبي يوسف والشافعي الله يجوز [۱] للفجر في النصف الأخير من الليل. (فيعاد لو أدنَ قبله ، ويؤذِّنُ عالماً بالأوقات لينالَ الثواب) : أي النواب" الذي وُعِدَ للمؤذنين. الدارقطني والبيهقي من رواية حفص بن أبي الغطاف، عن أبي الزناد عن الأعرج عن أبي هريرة مرفوعا : «من نسي صلاة فوقتها إذا ذكرها»، وحفص ضعيف جداً». [١]قوله : يجوز للفجر ؛ لقوله : «إنّ بلالاً يؤذن بليل فكلوا واشربوا حتى ينادي ابن أم مكتوم» (١) ، أخرجه أصحابُ الصحاح والسنن ، وحجة الجمهور أن الأذان إنما هو لإعلام دخول الوقتِ وحضور الصلاة، فلا معنى لتقديمه، وبه شهدت أخبار كثيرة. وأما هذا الحديث فالجواب عنه على ما أفاده الشيخ الأكبر) في «الفتوحات المكية»: إنّ أذان بلال كان ذكراً بصورة الأذان ولم يكن لصلاة الفجر ؛ ولذا احتيج إلى أذان آخر ، وفي المقام أبحاث بسطناها في «التعليق الممجد» و«السعاية». [٢] قوله : فيعاد ؛ تفريع على قوله : «في وقتها» ؛ أي فتجب إعادة الأذان إن أذن قبل الوقت، وكذا لو قدم بعض كلماته على الوقت ووقع بعضها في الوقت، يلزمُ استئناف الكلّ، وكذا تجب إعادة الإقامة قبل الوقت. [٣]قوله : أي الثواب ؛ أشار به إلى أنّ مطلق الثواب ليس منوطاً على كونه عالماً (۱) في (صحيح البخاري (۱) : (۲۲۳)، و (صحیح ابن حبان (٨: ٢٤٨)، وغيرها. (۲) وهو محمد بن علي بن محمد ابن عربي الحاتمي الطائي الأندلسي المالكي الصوفي، أبو بكر، محيي الدين، من مؤلفاته : الفتوحات المكية في معرفة أسرار المالكية والملكية»، و«جامع الأحكام في معرفة الحلال والحرام» و «فصوص الحكم ، قال اليافعي عن الطعن في ابن العربي : : إن أعظم ما يطعن الطاعنون فيه بسبب كتابه الموسوم بـ «فصوص الحكم»: وبلغني أن الإمام العلامة ابن الزملكاني شرح كتابه المذكور، ووجهه توجيهاً نفى عنه ما يظن من المحظور، ويخشى من الوقوع في المحذور .ا.هـ. ( ٥٦٠ - ٦٣٨هـ). ينظر : مرآة الجنان (٤) : ١٠٠ – ١٠١)، و«النجوم الزاهرة» (٦ : ٣٣٩ - ٣٤٠) ، و(الكشف (۲ : ۱۲۳۸ ، ۵۳۳).
Book of Prayer / Adhan 33: It is to be repeated if he calls the adhan before it (the time), and he should call the adhan knowing the times to attain the reward. So let him pray it when he remembers it, for that is its time. And according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them, it is permissible for Fajr in the last half of the night. (It is to be repeated if he calls the adhan before it, and he should call the adhan knowing the times to attain the reward): i.e., the reward promised for the mu'adhdhins. Al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi from the narration of Hafs ibn Abi al-Ghitaf, from Abu al-Zinad, from al-A'raj, from Abu Huraira, marfu': 'Whoever forgets a prayer, its time is when he remembers it', and Hafs is very weak. [Footnote 1] His statement: 'It is permissible for Fajr' because of his statement: 'Indeed Bilal calls the adhan at night, so eat and drink until Ibn Umm Maktum calls the adhan', reported by the authors of the Sahihs and Sunan. The proof of the majority is that the adhan is only for announcing the entry of the time and the presence of the prayer, so there is no meaning to its advancement, and many reports bear witness to this. As for this hadith, the answer to it according to what the Greatest Shaykh (Muhammad ibn al-Arabi) stated in 'al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya' is that Bilal's adhan was a dhikr in the form of adhan and was not for the Fajr prayer; therefore, another adhan was needed. In this place, there are investigations we have expanded upon in 'al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad' and 'al-Sa'aya'. [Footnote 2] His statement: 'It is to be repeated' is a branch on his statement 'in its time'; i.e., repeating the adhan is obligatory if he called the adhan before the time, and likewise if he advanced some of its words before the time and some occurred in the time, starting all over again is necessary, and likewise the iqama before the time must be repeated. [Footnote 3] His statement: 'i.e., the reward' indicates that absolute reward is not contingent on his being knowledgeable [of the times]. (Reference to Bukhari and Ibn Hibban).
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage deals with two main issues: (1) the ruling on adhan performed before its correct time, and (2) the disagreement regarding adhan for Fajr before dawn. The author states that the adhan must be repeated if called before the time, and that even if only part of it was before time, the entire adhan must be restarted. The iqama also must be repeated if called before time. This follows from the principle that adhan is for announcing the entry of the prayer time. Regarding Fajr, Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that it is permissible to call the adhan in the last half of the night, citing the hadith that Bilal used to call the adhan at night (before dawn). The majority (including Abu Hanifa) argue that the adhan is for informing of the entrance of the time, so there is no benefit in advancing it. They respond to the hadith by explaining that Bilal's adhan was not a proper adhan for Fajr but rather a dhikr in the form of an adhan to wake people up for suhur; hence, another adhan was needed (that of Ibn Umm Maktum). The passage also touches on the requirement that the mu'adhdhin be knowledgeable of the times; this is to ensure the adhan is given at the correct time, though the reward is not strictly dependent on knowledge but on proper timing.

Key Terms
يعاد (yu'ad): It must be repeated; an obligation to redo the adhan if given before the proper time.
النصف الأخير من الليل (al-nisf al-akhir min al-layl): The last half of the night, used as the time when Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i allow Fajr adhan.
ذكراً بصورة الأذان (dhikran bi-surat al-adhan): A remembrance in the form of adhan, used to explain Bilal's call; it was not a legal adhan for Fajr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a mu'adhdhin gives the adhan for Fajr before the true dawn?
A) It is valid and the prayer is permitted
B) It is invalid and must be repeated
C) It is makruh but valid
D) It is permissible with a valid reason

Key Takeaway
Adhan before its prescribed time is invalid and must be repeated; the pre-dawn Fajr adhan is not a proper adhan but a dhikr, so it does not count as the obligatory adhan for Fajr.

Rulings on Adhan: Time and Reward
Commentary on matn about repeating adhan and knowing times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on repeating the adhan if given before time, and explain the role of knowledge in attaining reward.

Core Idea
An adhan before its time is invalid and must be repeated; knowledge of times enhances reward but is not its basis.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains two key rulings from the Wiqaya matn: the necessity of repeating the adhan if performed prematurely, and the virtue of the mu'adhdhin who knows the prayer times. Understanding these points clarifies the legal weight of timing in the adhan and the spiritual merit of the caller.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the matn
The matn states: 'He repeats the call if he called before it, and he calls knowing the times to obtain reward.' These are two separate rulings.
The first is a legal obligation, the second a recommended virtue.
2
Understand the wajib status of i'aadah
The commentator explicitly says 'repetition of the adhan becomes obligatory (tajibu) if called before time.' This is a wajib ruling, making it a required act.
Note: if part of the adhan is before time and part within, the entire adhan must be restarted.
3
Distinguish between absolute reward and special promised reward
The commentator clarifies that the reward for mu'adhdhins is not conditional on knowledge; absolute reward is given for any valid adhan. However, the special rewards mentioned in hadith (e.g., longest necks, immunity from fire) are attained by those who call correctly and with knowledge.
Knowledge of times is a means to greater reward, not a condition for reward itself.
4
Recognize the hadith evidence for mu'adhdhin's merit
The commentator cites three hadith: longest necks, seven years of adhan grants immunity, and prayer for guidance and forgiveness. These establish the virtue but are not tied to the ruling on repetition.
These hadith encourage doing the adhan properly, reinforcing the need for correct timing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيعاد لو أذن قبله ، ويؤذن عالما بالأوقات لينال الثواب
[٢] قوله : فيعاد ؛ تفريع على قوله : «في وقتها» ؛ أي فتجب إعادة الأذان إن أذن قبل الوقت، وكذا لو قدم بعض كلماته على الوقت ووقع بعضها في الوقت، يلزمُ استئناف الكلّ، وكذا تجب إعادة الإقامة قبل الوقت.
[٣]قوله : أي الثواب ; أشار به إلى أنّ مطلق الثواب ليس منوطاً على كونه عالما ، بل الثواب الموعود للمؤذنين وفضلهم الوارد في الأحاديث : كحديث : «المؤذنون أطول الناس أعناقاً يوم القيامة) (۲) أخرجه مسلم ، وحديث : من أذن سبع سنين محتسباً كتبت له براءة من النار (۳) وحديث: «اللهم أرشد الأئمة واغفر للمؤذنين»(4) إلى غير ذلك.
He repeats the call if he called before it, and he calls knowing the times to obtain reward. [2] His saying: 'he repeats' is a branch on his saying: 'in its time'; i.e., repetition of the adhan becomes obligatory if he called before the time, and likewise if he presented some of its words before the time and some occurred in the time, the whole must be restarted, and likewise the repetition of the iqamah before the time is obligatory. [3] His saying: 'i.e., the reward' indicates that absolute reward is not conditional on him being knowledgeable, rather the promised reward for the mu'adhdhins and their virtue mentioned in hadith: like the hadith: 'The mu'adhdhins will have the longest necks on the Day of Resurrection' recorded by Muslim, and the hadith: 'Whoever calls the adhan for seven years seeking reward, a certificate of immunity from the Fire is written for him' and the hadith: 'O Allah, guide the imams and forgive the mu'adhdhins' etc.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Al-Wiqayah regarding two rulings for the adhan. The matn states: 'He repeats the call if he called before it, and he calls knowing the times to obtain reward.' The commentator explains the first part: 'repetition of the adhan is obligatory if the adhan was performed before the prescribed time. If some words were said before time and some within time, the entire adhan must be restarted. The same applies to the iqamah: if recited before time, it must be repeated. The second part of the matn is about the reward: the promise of reward for mu'adhdhins is not conditional on being knowledgeable about the times; rather, absolute reward is given for any dhikr of Allah. However, knowing the times is a means to attain the special reward mentioned in hadith, such as the hadith in Muslim that mu'adhdhins will have the longest necks on the Day of Resurrection, and other hadith about immunity from the Fire and forgiveness. The commentator emphasizes that the reward is not contingent on knowledge but is enhanced by it.

Key Terms
الإعادة (al-i'aadah): Repetition of the adhan or iqamah because the first was invalid due to being before the time.
الثواب (al-thawab): The divine reward promised to mu'adhdhins, achieved by performing the adhan correctly and with intention.
استئناف (al-isti'naf): Restarting the entire adhan from the beginning after an invalid attempt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mu'adhdhin gives the adhan for Fajr during the last half of the night (before dawn), what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The adhan is valid and does not need repetition.
B) The adhan must be repeated at the proper time.
C) The adhan is valid only if the mu'adhdhin is knowledgeable.
D) The adhan is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
An adhan given before the prescribed time is invalid and must be repeated; knowing the prayer times increases the mu'adhdhin's reward but is not a condition for basic validity.

Facing Qibla and Placing Fingers in Ears During Adhan
Explains two recommended acts for the mu'adhdhin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing qibla during adhan and identify the classification of placing fingers in ears, distinguishing between sunnah and mustahabb.

Core Idea
Facing qibla is sunnah; placing fingers in ears is mustahabb — both are recommended but not obligatory.

The Prophet's call to prayer (adhan) has certain recommended practices. Two of these are facing the qibla and placing the index fingers in the ears. While some think these are obligatory, the Hanafi school clarifies their actual status, distinguishing between confirmed sunnah and merely recommended acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts
What are the two actions discussed? Facing qibla and placing fingers in ears.
2
Determine the ruling classification for each
According to the text, facing qibla is sunnah; placing fingers in ears is mustahabb.
Sunnah omission is makruh; mustahabb omission is not disliked.
3
Examine the evidence
For facing qibla, the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd; for fingers, the Prophet's order to Bilal.
Both proofs are from ahad hadith, indicating recommendation.
4
Understand the consequence of omission
Omission of a sunnah is makruh tanzihi; omission of mustahabb is not disliked.
The adhan remains valid in both cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١]قوله : مستقبل القبلة ؛ هذا سنة ، فلو تركه جازَ الحصول المقصود، لكنه يكره. كذا في «الهداية»)، والأصل فيه هو ما ورد في رواية أحمد وأبي داود في قصة عبد الله ابن زيد الله ، ورؤيته رجلاً في المنام يُعلّمه الأذان أنه استقبل القبلةَ وأَذَن.
[٢]قوله : وأصبعاه في أذنيه ؛ المراد به أن يجعل المسبحتين من يديه في أذنيه ، به أمر رسولُ الله بلالاً قال: «إنه أرفع الصوتك ) ، أخرجه ابن ماجة وغيره، وهو أمر مستحب ليس من السنن الأصلية، وفي المقام كلام بسطناه في رسالتي : سباحة الفكر في الجهر بالذكر».
[1] His statement: Facing the qibla: This is sunnah. So if he abandons it, the intended purpose is achieved, but it is disliked. As in al-Hidayah. Its basis is what is reported in the narration of Ahmad and Abu Dawud in the story of Abdullah ibn Zayd (may Allah be pleased with him) and his vision of a man in a dream teaching him the adhan, that he faced the qibla and made the call. [2] His statement: And his fingers in his ears: What is meant is that he places the index fingers of his hands in his ears. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered Bilal to do so, saying: 'It raises your voice.' Reported by Ibn Majah and others. It is a recommended act, not from the original sunan, and there is discussion about it, which I have elaborated in my treatise: سباحة الفكر في الجهر بالذكر.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on two recommended acts of the adhan: facing the qibla and placing fingers in the ears. The author explains that facing the qibla is a sunnah act; omitting it does not invalidate the adhan but is makruh (disliked). He refers to al-Hidayah for this ruling. The proof comes from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd, who saw a man in a dream teaching the adhan with facing the qibla. As for placing the fingers in the ears, the author clarifies that the mu'adhdhin should place his index fingers (the سبابتان) in his ears. This was ordered by the Prophet to Bilal to increase the volume of the call. However, this is a mustahabb (recommended) act, not part of the original sunnah of adhan. The author mentions he has discussed this further in his own work. According to the Hanafi school, these acts are not obligatory but are meritorious.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; the Prophet did it consistently; omission is disliked (makruh tanzihi) but does not invalidate.
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended act; not from the original sunan; omission is not disliked.
مسبحتين (musabbahatayn): The index fingers; the fingers used to point during tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on facing the qibla during adhan according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is obligatory (fard).
B) It is sunnah; omitting it is makruh.
C) It is mustahabb; omitting it is permissible without dislike.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Facing qibla is a sunnah act, and placing fingers in ears is mustahabb; neither invalidates the adhan if omitted.

Tarsil, Lahn, and Tarji' in Adhan
Rulings on slow recitation, melodious voice, and returning in adhan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on tarsil, lahn, and tarji' in the adhan and explain the basis for the Hanafi rejection of tarji'.

Core Idea
Beautifying the voice in adhan is good as long as letters are unchanged; tarji' is rejected because Bilal did not practice it.

The adhan is a beautiful call to prayer, but its recitation is governed by precise rules. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies three key aspects: the recommended slow pace (tarsil), the prohibition of melodious alterations (lahn), and the debated practice of repeating the shahada in a lowered voice (tarji'). By understanding these rulings, you will grasp the Hanafi school's methodology in deriving adhan practices from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Tarsil (slow recitation), lahn (melodious alteration), and tarji' (lowering/raising voice in shahada). Also note the rule on beautifying the voice without alteration.
2
State the Hanafi position on each
Tarsil is sunnah; lahn (changing letters/vowels) is prohibited; beautifying without change is permissible (hasan); tarji' is not practiced.
The Hanafi position on tarji' is based on the practice of Bilal.
3
Identify the opponent's view
The Shafi'i school holds tarji' as a sunnah based on the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah.
4
Compare the dalil
Hanafi: Bilal's adhan witnessed by the Prophet, devoid of tarji'. Shafi'i: Abu Mahdhurah hadith teaching tarji'.
The Hanafi school prioritizes the witnessed practice over the isolated hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafis omit tarji'; Shafi'is include it. This affects how the mu'adhdhin recites the shahada.
The practical consequence is a difference in the manner of adhan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويَتَرَسلُ فيه بلا لَحْن وترجيع ... (ويَتَرَسلُ فيه) : أي يتمهل) ، (بلا لحن وترجيع): لَحْنَ في القراءة : طربَ وتَرَنَّمَ، مأخوذ من ألحان الأغاني، فلا ينقص شيئا من حروفه، ولا يزيد في أثنائه حرفا، وكذا لا يُنقص، ولا يزيد من كيفيات الحروف كالحركات والسكنات، والمدات ، وغير ذلك ؛ لتحسين الصوت بالأوقات، فإنه لا شك أن مَن يذكر الله يثاب عليه قطعاً، بل الثواب الموعود للمؤذنين وفضلهم الوارد في الأحاديث : كحديث : «المؤذنون أطول الناس أعناقاً يوم القيامة) (۲) أخرجه مسلم ، وحديث : من أذن سبع سنين محتسباً كتبت له براءة من النار (۳) وحديث: «اللهم أرشد الأئمة واغفر للمؤذنين»(4) إلى غير ذلك. ... [١]قوله : ويترسل ؛ الترسل هو التمهل، وهو أن يفصل بين كل كلمتين بسكتة من غير إسراع، والمسنون في الإقامة هو الإسراع ، لحديث: «إذا أذنت فترسل في أذانك ، وإذا أقمت فأحدر ) ؛ أي أسرع ، قاله النبي لبلال له ، أخرجه الترمذي. (۱) قوله : فإنه حسن ؛ لأنه مرفق ومؤثر، ولذا ورد الأمر في تلاوة القرآن ؛ لحديث: «زينوا القرآنُ بأصواتكم» (٢) ، وحدث : «ليس منا من لم يتغنَّ القرآن» (۳). [٢]قوله : والترجيع ؛ هو سنة عند الشافعي له وغيره ؛ لأنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم علم أبا محذورة الأذانَ بهذه الكيفية، وأصحابنا أخذوا بأذان بلال الذي كان يؤذن به بين يدي رسول الله حضراً وسفراً، فإنّه خال عن الترجيع، وكذا روايات قصة عبد الله بن زيد
And he recites slowly without melody and tarji'... (recites slowly): i.e., takes his time. (without melody and tarji'): lahn in recitation is to sing and melodize, taken from the melodies of songs. So he should not reduce anything from its letters, nor add a letter in its midst, and likewise he should not reduce or add from the qualities of letters such as vowels, sukoons, elongations, etc., to beautify the voice at times. Indeed, there is no doubt that whoever remembers Allah is certainly rewarded, rather the promised reward for the mu'adhdhins and their virtue mentioned in hadiths: like the hadith 'The mu'adhdhins will have the longest necks on the Day of Resurrection' (reported by Muslim), and the hadith 'Whoever calls the adhan for seven years seeking reward, it is written for him a release from the Fire', and the hadith 'O Allah, guide the imams and forgive the mu'adhdhins', etc. ... [1] His statement: and he recites slowly: tarsul is taking time, and it is that he separates between each two words with a pause without speed. And the sunnah in the iqama is speed, due to the hadith: 'When you make the adhan, recite slowly in your adhan, and when you make the iqama, be quick'; i.e., hasten, said by the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Bilal. Reported by al-Tirmidhi. [2] His statement: and it is good: because it is pleasing and effective, hence the command in the recitation of the Qur'an is reported, due to the hadith: 'Adorn the Qur'an with your voices', and the hadith: 'He is not of us who does not chant the Qur'an'. [3] His statement: and tarji': it is sunnah according to al-Shafi'i and others, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) taught Abu Mahdhurah the adhan with this manner. Our companions (Hanafis) have taken the adhan of Bilal, who used to call the adhan before the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) while traveling and in residence, and it was devoid of tarji'. Similarly, the narrations of the story of Abdullah ibn Zayd.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage covers three related rulings: tarsil (slow recitation), lahn (melody), and tarji' (repeating the shahada in a lowered then raised voice). The author begins by stating the main text: the mu'adhdhin should recite slowly without lahn or tarji'. He then explains tarsil as taking pauses between phrases, while the iqama should be recited quickly. On lahn, he clarifies that it refers to singing or altering the letters/qualities of letters; simply beautifying the voice without changing pronunciation is good (hasan), supported by hadiths on reciting the Qur'an beautifully. The major point of dispute is tarji': Imam al-Shafi'i considers it a sunnah based on the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah, while the Hanafis follow the practice of Bilal, who did not do tarji'. The Hanafi response is that the authentic sunnah is the practice of Bilal, which was witnessed by the Prophet. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that Hanafis do not practice tarji', whereas Shafi'is do. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is to omit tarji'.

Key Terms
الترسل (al-tarsul): Slow, measured recitation with pauses between phrases.
اللحن (al-lahn): Melodious alteration of letters or vowels; singing in a way that changes the words.
الترجيع (al-tarji'): Lowering the voice while saying the shahada, then raising it again.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis reject the practice of tarji' in the adhan?
A) Because it is melodious.
B) Because it was not practiced by Bilal in the presence of the Prophet.
C) Because it is from the iqama.
D) Because it requires turning the face.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school emphasizes adhering to the practice of Bilal in the adhan, rejecting tarji' and allowing beautification of voice as long as no letters are altered.

Turning the Face During the Hay'alatayn
Ruling on turning the face in adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on turning the face during the hay'alatayn and identify its basis in the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The mu'adhdhin turns his face right and left during the hay'alatayn as a sunnah, following Bilal's practice.

In the adhan, the mu'adhdhin calls the people to prayer. When he says 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', he turns his face to indicate direction. This lesson explains the ruling and manner of this turning, based on the practice of the Prophet's mu'adhdhin, Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him). The Hanafi school holds it as a sunnah act, not an obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
Recognize that turning the face during the hay'alatayn is part of the adhan. Determine its legal status: sunnah, not fard or wajib.
The text explicitly derives this from the action of Bilal.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence in the text: the report of Bilal's practice, authenticated by Bukhari. This is a dalil naqli (textual proof).
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, indicating its strong authenticity.
3
Understand the manner (kayfiyya)
Note the specific directions: at 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' turn right, at 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' turn left. Only the face and neck turn, not the whole body.
This distinction is important to avoid exaggeration.
4
Apply the ruling
In practice, the mu'adhdhin should follow this sunnah. If omitted, the adhan remains valid but one misses a recommended act.
No compensation (like sajdah al-sahw) is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ويُحوِّل وجهَهُ في الخَيْعلتين يَمْنةً ويَسْرة ... [٣]قوله : ويحوّل ؛ من التحويل ؛ أي يصرفُ وجهه يميناً عند : حي على الصلاة، وشمالاً عند حي على الفلاح (4) ؛ لأنه خطاب ، فينبغي أن يواجه به القوم، وهو المروي من فعل بلال () الله أخرجه البخاري وغيره. [٤] قوله : في الحيعلتين ؛ تثنية حيعلة ، بفتح الحاء، وتشديد الياء المفتوحة، وهو مصدر حيعل ؛ أي قال : حي على الصلاة، حي على الفلاح.
And he turns his face during the two hay'alahs to the right and left... [3] His statement: and he turns: from conversion; meaning he directs his face to the right at 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and to the left at 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'; because it is a call (addressing people), so he should face the people. This is the reported action of Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him), recorded by Bukhari and others. [4] His statement: during the two hay'alahs: dual of hay'alah, with fatha on ha' and tashdid on ya' with fatha, a verbal noun of hay'ala; i.e., he says 'Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah'.

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on the mu'adhdhin turning his face during the two phrases 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'. The author confirms that it is a sunnah act. The mu'adhdhin should turn his face to the right when saying 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and to the left when saying 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'. The reason is that these are calls to the people, so the mu'adhdhin should face the direction he is addressing. This practice is reported from Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him) and is recorded by Imam Bukhari and others. The author also explains the term 'hay'alah' as a verbal noun from 'hay'ala', meaning to say the calls. According to the Hanafi school, this turning is a sunnah and should be done without turning the entire body; only the neck and face turn. Some narrations indicate he turned his neck but did not turn his chest.

Key Terms
الحيعلة (al-hay'alah): The phrase 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'.
تحويل الوجه (tahwil al-wajh): Turning the face to the right and left during the call.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He turns to the left.
B) He turns to the right.
C) He faces the qibla.
D) He turns his back to the qibla.

Key Takeaway
Turning the face during the hay'alatayn is a sunnah based on the action of Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him), recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari, and only the face and neck should turn.

The Ruling on Tarji' in the Shahadatayn: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on tarji' in adhan shahadatayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on tarji' in the adhan and identify the primary evidence each school relies upon.

Core Idea
Tarji' in the shahadatayn is a sunnah for Shafi'is but not practiced by Hanafis, who follow Bilal's adhan.

The adhan is a distinctive ritual of Islam, yet details such as the manner of reciting the shahadatayn have been debated among the schools. This passage presents the core dispute over tarji', the practice of repeating the shahadah first quietly then loudly. You will learn the evidence and reasoning of each school, and understand the practical difference in the adhan as performed in Hanafi and Shafi'i mosques.

Guided Path
1
Define tarji' in the adhan context
Understand that tarji' means to say the shahadatayn first in a lowered voice, then repeat them in a raised voice. This is the specific technique under dispute.
2
Identify the two positions
State clearly: the Hanafi school does not practice tarji' in the adhan; the Shafi'i school considers it a sunnah.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafis rely on the adhan of Bilal, which was performed in the presence of the Prophet (saw) without tarji', and the dream of Abdullah ibn Zaid which described the adhan without tarji'.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'is rely on the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah, where the Prophet (saw) taught him the adhan with tarji'.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis argue that Bilal's practice is more continuous and normative; the Abu Mahdhurah hadith is specific to one situation and does not abrogate the established practice.
6
Understand the practical difference
In a Hanafi mosque, the mu'adhdhin says the shahadatayn once in one tone. In a Shafi'i mosque, he first says them quietly then repeats loudly. The difference is visible to the listener.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما مجرد تحسين الصوت بلا تغيير لفظ فإنه حسن، والترجيع في الشهادتين أن يخفض بهما، ثم يرفع الصوت بهما.
قوله : والترجيع ; هو سنة عند الشافعي له وغيره؛ لأنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم علم أبا محذورة الأذانَ بهذه الكيفية، وأصحابنا أخذوا بأذان بلال الذي كان يؤذن به بين يدي رسول الله حضراً وسفراً، فإنّه خال عن الترجيع، وكذا روايات قصة عبد الله بن زيد.
As for merely beautifying the voice without changing the wording, it is good. And tarji' in the two shahadatayn is to lower the voice with them, then raise the voice with them. He said: 'And tarji''; it is sunnah according to al-Shafi'i and others because the Prophet taught Abu Mahdhurah the adhan in this manner. And our companions (Hanafis) took the adhan of Bilal which he used to give in the presence of the Messenger of Allah, both on journeys and at home, and it was free from tarji', and likewise the narrations of the story of Abdullah ibn Zaid.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage addresses two related issues. First, merely beautifying the voice without altering the wording is considered good (hasan). Second, the main issue is the definition and ruling of tarji' in the shahadatayn of the adhan. Tarji' means to say the shahadah in a low voice first and then repeat it in a raised voice. The Shafi'i school, based on the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah, considers this a sunnah. However, the Hanafi school follows the practice of Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him), who gave the adhan in the presence of the Prophet without tarji'. Also, the story of Abdullah ibn Zaid, who saw the adhan in a dream, confirms the adhan without tarji'. Therefore, Hanafis do not practice tarji' in the shahadatayn; it is not part of their adhan. The author clarifies that this is a clear disagreement between the schools.

Key Terms
الترجيع (al-tarji'): In adhan, to say the shahadatayn first in a lowered voice, then repeat them in a raised voice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sunnah
B) Mandatory
C) Not practiced
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not incorporate tarji' in the adhan, following the established practice of Bilal, while the Shafi'i school regards it as sunnah based on the instruction to Abu Mahdhurah.

Turning the Face and Istidarah in Adhan
Commentary on turning face and istidarah in adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on turning the face during adhan and determine when istidarah (full body turn) is required.

Core Idea
Turning the face at 'hayya ala al-salah' and 'hayya ala al-falah' is a sunnah; if the minaret prevents notification, the mu'adhdhin must use istidarah.

The adhan is a call to prayer, and its performance includes certain sunan to ensure the congregation is addressed properly. One of these sunan is turning the face at the two hay'alatayn. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence from the practice of Bilal, and the practical necessity of istidarah when the minaret does not allow effective notification through turning alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that turning the face during the adhan is a sunnah mu'akkadah. Identify the two points at which the mu'adhdhin turns: 'hayya ala al-salah' (right) and 'hayya ala al-falah' (left).
This ruling is derived from the text's explicit statement and the practice of Bilal.
2
Locate the dalil
Recall the proof cited: the action of Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him) as narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari. Note that this is a companion practice approved by the Prophet.
The Hanafi school accepts such practices as evidence for sunnah.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain why the action of Bilal indicates sunnah: because the Prophet (peace be upon him) heard Bilal's adhan and did not object, thus tacitly approving it. This establishes the sunnah of turning.
The dalala is zanni, so it establishes sunnah, not wajib.
4
Identify the condition for istidarah
Understand that if the minaret is such that turning the face alone does not allow the mu'adhdhin's voice to reach the congregation, then he must turn his whole body (istidarah) by moving from one window to another.
Istidarah is not an independent sunnah but a practical necessity.
5
Resolve the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that some scholars suggested turning the face both right and left in each hay'alah, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to turn once per hay'alah, as upheld by al-Khayr al-Ramli and the majority of Hanafi authorities.
The alternative view was considered weak as it contradicts the authentic transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحوِّل وجهَهُ في الخَيْعلتين يَمْنةً ويَسِّرة
قوله : ويحوّل ; من التحويل ; أي يصرفُ وجهه يميناً عند : حي على الصلاة، وشمالاً عند حي على الفلاح ; لأنه خطاب ، فينبغي أن يواجه به القوم، وهو المروي من فعل بلال أخرجه البخاري وغيره.
قوله : في الحيعلتين ; تثنية حيعلة ، بفتح الحاء، وتشديد الياء المفتوحة، وهو مصدر حيعل ; أي قال : حي على الصلاة، حي على الفلاح.
ويستدير في صومعته إن لم يمكن التحويل مع الثبات في مكانه) : المراد أنه إذا كان المئذنة بحيث لو حول وجهَهُ مع ثباتِ قدميه لا يحصل الإعلام، فحينئذ يستدير فيها، فيخرجُ رأسَهُ من الكوة اليمنى، ويقول : حي على الصلاة ثُمَّ يذهب إلى الكَوَّة اليُسرى ، ويُخْرِجُ رأسه ، ويقول : حي على الفلاح.
قوله : صومعته ; هي الموضعُ العالي على رأس المئذنة، وهي في الأصل متعبد النصارى ، قاله العيني
قوله : بحيث لو حول وجهه ; لَمَّا استشعر بما في كلام المصنف له من الإشكال بأنه كيف لا يمكن تحويلُ الوجه مع ثباتِ قدميه في موضعه أشار إلى دفعه بأنّ المقصود نفي التحويل الذي يحصل به الإعلام.
قوله : ثم يذهب ; هذا هو الأصح ; كما في «البناية» و«التبيين») و«المنية» وغيرها، وقيل: يحول وجهه في كلّ من الحيعلتين مرَّة يُمنةً ومرة يُسرة، قال ابن الهمام : هو الأوجه ، ورده الخيرُ الرملي بأنه مخالف للصحيح المنقول عن السلف.
And he turns his face in the two hay'alatayn to the right and left. He said: 'Yuhawwil' from tahwil; meaning he directs his face to the right at 'hayya ala al-salah' and to the left at 'hayya ala al-falah' because it is an address, so he should face the people, and this is reported from the action of Bilal, narrated by al-Bukhari and others. He said: 'fi al-hay'alatayn' is the dual of hay'alah, with fath of the ha and tashdid of the ya, it is a masdar of hay'ala, meaning he said: hayya ala al-salah, hayya ala al-falah. And he turns around in his minaret if turning the face while remaining in place is not possible: the meaning is that if the minaret is such that if he turns his face while his feet remain fixed, notification is not achieved, then in that case he turns around in it, so he puts his head out of the right window and says: hayya ala al-salah, then he goes to the left window and puts out his head and says: hayya ala al-falah. He said: 'sumu'atihi' is the high place at the top of the minaret, originally it is the place of worship of the Christians, as stated by al-Ayni. He said: 'bi-haythu law hawwala wajhahu' - when the commentator sensed the objection in the author's words that how can turning the face not be possible while feet are fixed in place, he indicated its repudiation by saying that the intended meaning is the negation of the turning that achieves notification. He said: 'thumma yadhhab' - this is the most correct; as in al-Binaya, al-Tabyin, al-Munyah and others, and it is said that he turns his face in each of the two hay'alatayn once to the right and once to the left, Ibn al-Humam said it is the most appropriate, but al-Khayr al-Ramli refuted it as contradicting the sound transmission from the predecessors.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of the mu'adhdhin's turning his face during the adhan. The author explains that at the phrase 'hayya ala al-salah' the mu'adhdhin turns his face to the right, and at 'hayya ala al-falah' he turns to the left, because the call is an address to the people. This is proven from the practice of Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him) as recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari. The author then defines 'hay'alah' as the phrase 'hayya ala al-salah' and 'hayya ala al-falah'. If turning the face alone is insufficient for the people to hear (e.g., if the minaret is oriented such that turning the face does not direct the sound properly), then the mu'adhdhin should turn his entire body in the minaret, moving from one window to another. The commentary clarifies that 'sumu'ah' is the high structure at the top of the minaret, and notes the objection that it seems impossible not to be able to turn the face while the feet remain fixed. The author resolves this by explaining that the intended meaning is the turning that actually achieves notification, not just any turning. Finally, there is a difference of opinion: the correct position is that the mu'adhdhin goes from one window to the next, but some said he should turn his face both right and left in each hay'alah. Ibn al-Humam considered the latter more appropriate, but al-Khayr al-Ramli rejected it as opposed to the authentic transmission from the Salaf.

Key Terms
الحيعلة (al-hay'alah): The phrase 'hayya ala al-salah' or 'hayya ala al-falah'; a masdar from hay'ala; used in adhan.
الصومعة (al-sumu'ah): A high place on top of a minaret where the mu'adhdhin stands; originally a place of worship for Christians.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To the right
B) To the left
C) Straight ahead
D) To the qibla

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah for adhan is to turn right at 'hayya ala al-salah' and left at 'hayya ala al-falah', with istidarah only when turning the face fails to achieve notification.

Placement of 'al-Salatu Khayrun min al-Nawm' in Fajr Adhan
Dispute on placement of phrase in adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on when to say 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' during the Fajr adhan and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its placement.

Core Idea
The phrase 'Prayer is better than sleep' is said during the adhan, not after it.

In the Fajr adhan, the mu'adhdhin adds the phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm'. The Hanafi school holds that this phrase is said after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. However, some later Hanafi scholars argued it should be said after the adhan. This lesson clarifies the established position and the rebuttal of the alternative view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: the phrase is said after 'hayya 'ala al-falah' (after the falah of Fajr).
2
Identify the opposing view
Some mashayikh (later scholars) held that it should be said after the adhan is completely finished. Imam Muhammad's wording in al-Muwatta appears to support this.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author states he has refuted that view elsewhere, indicating that the correct position is the one in the matn.
The full refutation is not included in this passage, but the author's stance is clear.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the phrase is said after the adhan, a sunnah is missed, but the adhan remains valid. The mu'tamad is to say it during.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقول: بعد فلاح الفجر ; ذهب بعض المشايخ إلى أنّ محلَّ الصلاة خير من النوم بعد تمام الأذان ، وإليه يميل كلام الإمام محمد الله في «الموطأ»، وقد رددته عليه في
And he says: after the falah of Fajr; some mashayikh held that the place of 'as-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is after the completion of the adhan, and the words of Imam Muhammad in al-Muwatta incline towards this, and I have refuted this in...
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage discusses the placement of the phrase 'as-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' (Prayer is better than sleep) in the Fajr adhan. The matn states 'after the falah of Fajr', meaning after saying 'hayya ala al-falah'. However, some later mashayikh (scholars) held that this phrase should be said after the adhan is completely finished, not during it. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's wording in his narration of al-Muwatta seems to incline toward this view. The author (commentator) says he has refuted this position elsewhere, indicating that the correct Hanafi position is to say 'as-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' during the adhan, after 'hayya ala al-falah', based on the practice of Bilal and other companions. Unfortunately, the text cuts off, so the full rebuttal is not included here.

Key Terms
بعد فلاح الفجر (ba'da falah al-fajr): After saying 'hayya ala al-falah' in the Fajr adhan, the phrase 'as-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is said.
مشايخ (mashayikh): Later Hanafi scholars who held a differing view on the placement.
معتمد (mu'tamad): The relied-upon, authoritative position in the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only on Fridays

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi practice is to say 'as-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' after 'hayya ala al-falah' during the adhan, not after its completion.

The Mu'adhdhin's Turning in the Minaret
Explanation of the mu'adhdhin's movement when the minaret does not allow head-turning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mu'adhdhin's movement in the minaret and distinguish the mufta bihi position from the contrary view of Ibn al-Humam.

Core Idea
When the minaret prevents notification by head-turning, the mu'adhdhin must move to different windows.

The adhan is a call to prayer that must reach all directions. In minarets with multiple windows, the mu'adhdhin may not be able to face all sides simply by turning his neck while staying in one spot. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the Hanafi solution: he physically moves to different windows, facing each direction directly. It also addresses an alternative view and clarifies the relied-upon practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mu'adhdhin's turning during adhan from a minaret. The ruling is that he should turn around in his cell (صومعة) if necessary.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, part of the recommended method of adhan.
2
Identify the triggering condition
The condition is that turning his face while feet are fixed does not achieve notification (i'lam) to all directions. This depends on the minaret's structure.
If head-turning suffices, he does not need to move.
3
Describe the prescribed method
The mu'adhdhin takes out his head from the right window and says 'hayya 'ala al-salah', then goes to the left window and says 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.
This ensures facing the right and left directions respectively.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Ibn al-Humam considered turning the face left and right for each phrase as more appropriate, but al-Khayr al-Ramli rejected this as contrary to authentic practice from the salaf.
The mufta bihi is moving to windows, as confirmed in al-Binayah and other authoritative texts.
5
Apply the ruling practically
A mu'adhdhin in a minaret with windows on multiple sides should use the method of moving to windows when head-turning is insufficient.
This achieves the purpose of the adhan: widespread notification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستدير في صومعته إن لم يمكن التحويل مع الثبات في مكانه، ويقول : بعد فلاح (ويستدير في صومعته إن لم يمكن التحويل مع الثبات في مكانه) : المراد أنه إذا كان المئذنة بحيث لو حول وجهه مع ثبات قدميه لا يحصل الإعلام، فحينئذ يستدير فيها، فيخرج رأسه من الكوة اليمنى، ويقول : حي على الصلاة ثم يذهب إلى الكوة اليسرى، ويخرج رأسه، ويقول : حي على الفلاح. [1] قوله : صومعته؛ هي الموضع العالي على رأس المئذنة، وهي في الأصل متعبد النصارى، قاله العيني [2] قوله : بحيث لو حول وجهه؛ لما استشعر بما في كلام المصنف له من الإشكال بأنه كيف لا يمكن تحويل الوجه مع ثبات قدميه في موضعه أشار إلى دفعه بأن المقصود نفي التحويل الذي يحصل به الإعلام. [3] قوله : ثم يذهب؛ هذا هو الأصح؛ كما في «البناية» و«التبيين» و«المنية» وغيرها، وقيل: يحول وجهه في كل من الحيعلتين مرة يمنة ومرة يسرة، قال ابن الهمام : هو الأوجه، ورده الخير الرملي بأنه مخالف للصحيح المنقول عن السلف.
He turns around in his cell if turning (the face) with stability in his place is not possible, and he says: after success. (He turns around in his cell if turning with stability in his place is not possible): the meaning is that if the minaret is such that if he turns his face while his feet are fixed, the notification is not achieved, then he turns around in it, so he takes out his head from the right window and says: 'Come to prayer', then he goes to the left window and takes out his head and says: 'Come to success'. [1] His saying: his cell; it is the high place on top of the minaret, and originally it is a place of worship of the Christians, said by al-Ayni. [2] His saying: such that if he turns his face; when he sensed the objection in the author's words that how can turning the face be impossible while his feet are fixed in his place, he pointed to its rebuttal that the intent is to negate the turning that achieves notification. [3] His saying: then he goes; this is the most correct, as in al-Binayah, al-Tabyin, al-Munyah and others, and it is said: he turns his face in each of the two phrases once to the right and once to the left; Ibn al-Humam said: it is more appropriate, and al-Khayr al-Ramli rejected it saying it contradicts the authentic transmitted from the predecessors.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school on the proper method for a mu'adhdhin to call the adhan from a minaret that does not allow him to face all directions simply by turning his head while standing still. The ruling requires him to physically move to different windows, facing each direction separately. The commentary explains key terms: 'صومعة' (the high cell atop a minaret, originally a place of Christian worship), clarifies that 'turning' here means turning that achieves notification, not merely turning the neck. The most correct view, as confirmed in authoritative texts like al-Binayah and al-Tabyin, is that he moves to windows. An alternative view suggests turning the face left and right for each phrase, but this is rejected by al-Khayr al-Ramli as contrary to authentic transmitted practice from the salaf.

Key Terms
صومعة (sawma'ah): The high place on top of the minaret where the mu'adhdhin stands; originally a place of Christian worship.
كوة (kuwwah): A window or opening in the wall of the minaret.
حي على الصلاة (hayya 'ala al-salah): The phrase in adhan meaning 'Come to prayer'.
حي على الفلاح (hayya 'ala al-falah): The phrase in adhan meaning 'Come to success'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what should the mu'adhdhin do if turning his face while standing still does not achieve notification to all directions?
A) Turn his face left and right for each phrase.
B) Move to different windows of the minaret.
C) Climb down and call from the ground.
D) Raise his voice louder without moving.

Key Takeaway
The mu'adhdhin must physically move to different windows when head-turning from a fixed spot fails to notify all directions, following the sunnah method confirmed by Hanafi authorities.
